
Beginning on 28 February 2026, [Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel "Israel") and the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States") engaged in coordinated joint attacks on various sites in [Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran "Iran"), starting a major war aimed at a [regime change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regime_change "Regime change").[^80] [^81] Codenamed **Operation Roaring Lion** [^24] by Israel [^82] [^83] and **Operation Epic Fury** by the United States,[^84] [^85] [^86] the attacks have targeted key Iranian officials, military commanders, and facilities.[^87] Iran's response has been named **Operation True Promise IV**.[^25] [^26]

The operation began with joint strikes by Israel and the US in the cities of [Tehran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tehran "Tehran"), [Isfahan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isfahan "Isfahan"), [Qom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qom "Qom"), [Karaj](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karaj "Karaj"), and [Kermanshah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kermanshah "Kermanshah"). The attacks included [the assassination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Ali_Khamenei "Assassination of Ali Khamenei") of Supreme Leader [Ali Khamenei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Khamenei "Ali Khamenei"), [whose compound](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Office_of_the_Supreme_Leader_of_Iran "Office of the Supreme Leader of Iran") was destroyed; [Ali Shamkhani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Shamkhani "Ali Shamkhani"), former secretary of Iran's [Supreme National Security Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_National_Security_Council "Supreme National Security Council"); and [several other Iranian officials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Iranian_officials_killed_during_the_2026_Iran_conflict "List of Iranian officials killed during the 2026 Iran conflict").[^84] [^88] In retaliation, Iran launched dozens of [its drones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicles_in_the_Iranian_military "Unmanned aerial vehicles in the Iranian military") and [ballistic missiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ballistic_missiles "Ballistic missiles") throughout the [Persian Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf "Persian Gulf") at targets in Israel [^89] and US military bases **[^89]** in [Jordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan "Jordan"), [Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait "Kuwait"),[^90] [Bahrain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bahrain "Bahrain"),[^90] [Qatar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar "Qatar"),[^90] [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq"),[^91] [Saudi Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia "Saudi Arabia"),[^92] and the [United Arab Emirates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates "United Arab Emirates").[^93] Iran launched strikes on civilian airports and shipping ports in Kuwait, the UAE, [Oman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oman "Oman"),[^94] [^95] [^96] and Azerbaijan.[^97] Britain's [Akrotiri and Dhekelia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia "Akrotiri and Dhekelia") military base on [Cyprus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geography_of_Cyprus "Geography of Cyprus") was struck.[^98] [Iran closed the Strait of Hormuz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Strait_of_Hormuz_crisis "2026 Strait of Hormuz crisis"), disrupting global oil and gas shipments.[^99] [Hezbollah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hezbollah "Hezbollah") in [Lebanon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanon "Lebanon") joined the war after the killing of Khamenei.[^100] [^101] [^102]

The US made the attack without a clear plan,[^103] [^104] [^105] and US officials, including President [Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump "Donald Trump"), have offered various and shifting reasons for launching the war on Iran, including to ward off an imminent threat it poses, destroy [missile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ballistic_missile_program_of_Iran "Ballistic missile program of Iran") and [military capabilities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_of_Iran "Military of Iran"), prevent it from [obtaining nuclear weapons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_program_of_Iran "Nuclear program of Iran"), and ultimately to [achieve regime change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_involvement_in_regime_change "United States involvement in regime change") by bringing the [Iranian opposition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_opposition "Iranian opposition") to power.[^106] [^107] Iran rejected US claims that it was preparing an attack.[^108] After the strikes, the [International Atomic Energy Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency "International Atomic Energy Agency") said that Iran does not have a nuclear weapons program.[^109] [^110] [^111] [^112] The [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations") and several uninvolved countries, including [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China") and [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia "Russia"), condemned the initial strikes for undermining the stability of the Middle East; others condemned Iran's retaliatory strikes on US allies in the region.[^113] Critics of the operation described it as illegal under US law,[^114] an act of [imperialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_imperialism "American imperialism"),[^115] [^116] and a violation of Iran's [sovereignty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sovereignty "Sovereignty") [^117] [^118] under [international law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_law "International law").[^119]

## Background

A US and UK-backed [coup d'etat in 1953](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1953_Iranian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1953 Iranian coup d'état") deposed Prime Minister [Mohammad Mosaddegh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Mosaddegh "Mohammad Mosaddegh") and strengthened the rule of [Mohammad Reza Pahlavi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Reza_Pahlavi "Mohammad Reza Pahlavi"), the [shah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shah "Shah").[^120] [^121] [^122] Resentment of the shah's deference to Western interests and his [autocratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autocracy "Autocracy") monarchical rule led to the [1979 revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1979_revolution "1979 revolution") in which he was overthrown,[^120] [^123] [^124] and after which Iran became an [Islamic republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_republic "Islamic republic") and severed diplomatic ties with the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States") [^120] [^125] and Israel.[^126]

During the [Iran–Iraq War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War "Iran–Iraq War") in the 1980s, the US [provided](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_support_for_Iraq_during_the_Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War "United States support for Iraq during the Iran–Iraq War") economic, intelligence, and indirect military support to Iraq. Iran has supported an informal [Axis of Resistance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axis_of_Resistance "Axis of Resistance") committed primarily to countering the influence of the US and Israel in the Middle East, engaging in [proxy conflicts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proxy_war "Proxy war") in the region. These on-going tensions escalated into direct conflict between the US and Iran in January 2020 when President Donald Trump, during his first term, ordered the [assassination of Qasem Soleimani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Qasem_Soleimani "Assassination of Qasem Soleimani"), a senior [Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Revolutionary_Guard_Corps "Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps") commander.[^120] [^127]

Tensions between Iran and the US and Israel further escalated following the start of the [Gaza war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_war "Gaza war"), during which Israel weakened Iranian-backed militias across the Middle East, including [Hamas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamas "Hamas") in Gaza,[^27] [Hezbollah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hezbollah "Hezbollah") in Lebanon, and others. Israel and Iran [exchanged strikes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Iran%E2%80%93Israel_conflict "2024 Iran–Israel conflict") in April and October 2024, and were engaged in [a 12-day war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twelve-Day_War "Twelve-Day War") in June 2025 that included [an American airstrike](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_strikes_on_Iranian_nuclear_sites "United States strikes on Iranian nuclear sites") aimed at destroying Iran's nuclear facilities.[^130]

### Iran nuclear issue

[Iran's development of nuclear enrichment capabilities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_program_of_Iran "Nuclear program of Iran") has been an international controversy for decades, with the US and its allies seeking to prevent Iranian nuclear weapons development.[^131] [^132] Iran said it is not seeking nuclear weapons, and that its enrichment efforts are to generate [nuclear power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_power "Nuclear power") for civilian use.[^133] The Director General of the [International Atomic Energy Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency "International Atomic Energy Agency") (IAEA) said that there is no proof Iran is building an atomic bomb.[^134] [^110] [^111] [^112] The [United States withdrawal from the Joint Comprehensive Plan of Action](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_withdrawal_from_the_Joint_Comprehensive_Plan_of_Action "United States withdrawal from the Joint Comprehensive Plan of Action") in 2018 [^135] [^136] led to the re-imposition of [sanctions on Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanctions_on_Iran "Sanctions on Iran") and a turn towards the use of force rather than diplomacy in relations between the US and its allies and Iran. The [first Trump administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Trump_administration "First Trump administration") adopted a " [maximum pressure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximum_pressure_campaign "Maximum pressure campaign") " strategy.[^137] The [Biden administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biden_administration "Biden administration") did not relax the economic sanctions against Iran, and instead implemented more measures.[^138] The [second Trump administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Trump_administration "Second Trump administration") reimposed the "maximum pressure" approach on Iran.[^139] [^136]

The [Defense Intelligence Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defense_Intelligence_Agency "Defense Intelligence Agency") concluded in 2025 it would be a decade before Iran would be able to gain the technical skill to produce an arsenal of missiles that could reach the United States;[^87] the [United States Department of Defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense "United States Department of Defense") estimated Iran's nuclear programme had been set back by two years following earlier [strikes on Iranian nuclear sites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_strikes_on_Iranian_nuclear_sites "United States strikes on Iranian nuclear sites") in June 2025.[^140] In January 2026 US and European officials said Washington had presented Iran with three core demands, one of which was a permanent end to all uranium enrichment. [^141]

The Trump administration stated in February 2026 that Iran had restarted its nuclear programme and was developing missiles with enough range for an attack on the US.[^142] On 27 February 2026, the [International Atomic Energy Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency "International Atomic Energy Agency") (IAEA) discovered that Iran had hidden [highly enriched uranium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Highly_enriched_uranium "Highly enriched uranium") in an underground facility that was undamaged in the previous round of fighting,[^143] [^144] and IAEA said that they could not be sure that Iran's nuclear programme was "exclusively peaceful" at the time of reportage as the agency was denied access.[^145] According to an anonymous US source, Trump authorized the strike after the US received intelligence that Iran was planning to preemptively launch missiles.[^146] [^147] The administration did not provide any evidence that Iran was planning to preemptively strike US assets,[^148] and an unspecified Pentagon source told Congress in closed-door briefings that there was no intelligence suggesting Iran was planning to attack US forces first.[^149] [^150]

## Prelude

### Anti-government protests in Iran and initial US deployments

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Iran_protests_8_January_2026.jpg/250px-Iran_protests_8_January_2026.jpg)

Protests in Tehran on 8 January 2026. US president Donald Trump encouraged protests and threatened immediate military intervention if Iran killed peaceful protesters, but held off from it afterward despite massacres of protesters.

Beginning in late December 2025, massive [nationwide anti-government protests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2025%E2%80%932026_Iranian_protests "2025–2026 Iranian protests") erupted in Iran, driven largely by economic crisis, the collapse of the [rial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_rial "Iranian rial"), and rising prices. The protests, which included calls for regime change, became the largest in scale since the 1979 revolution.[^151] The Iranian government responded with [massacres of protesters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iran_massacres "2026 Iran massacres"), with the deadliest incidents occurring on 8 and 10 January 2026.[^152] In February 2026, US treasury secretary [Scott Bessent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scott_Bessent "Scott Bessent") claimed that Washington engineered a dollar shortage in Iran to send the Iranian rial into freefall and cause protests in Iran.[^153] [^154] [^155] The US-based [Human Rights Activists News Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Rights_Activists_News_Agency "Human Rights Activists News Agency") estimated the death toll at 7,000, the Iranian government said the death toll was 3,117, while Donald Trump and others said the death toll was 32,000 people.[^156] [^157]

On 2 January 2026, Trump threatened a "lock and loaded" military intervention in Iran if the government decided to kill peaceful protesters.[^158] On 13 January, he expressed support for Iranian anti-government protesters and pledged that "help is on the way" for them,[^159] and later, on 23 January, Trump announced that a US "armada" was heading to the Middle East, including the aircraft carrier [USS *Abraham Lincoln*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USS_Abraham_Lincoln_\(CVN-72\) "USS Abraham Lincoln (CVN-72)") and several guided-missile destroyers.[^160] [^161] On 13 February, Trump ordered the aircraft carrier [USS *Gerald R. Ford*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USS_Gerald_R._Ford "USS Gerald R. Ford") and its supporting warships to sail to the Middle East.[^162]

### 2026 nuclear negotiations

       <video controls="" width="201" height="113"><source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/f6/President_Trump_Gaggles_with_Press_Before_Departing_the_White_House%2C_Feb._27%2C_2026.webm/President_Trump_Gaggles_with_Press_Before_Departing_the_White_House%2C_Feb._27%2C_2026.webm.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; President Trump briefly discusses the United States' relationship with Iran with the press on 27 February, roughly 24 hours before the war begins.

On 6 February 2026, Iran and the US held indirect nuclear negotiations in [Oman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oman "Oman") 's capital, [Muscat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muscat "Muscat"). Iran emphasized that progress depends on consultations back in capitals.[^163] A second round of nuclear talks was scheduled in Geneva.[^163] Between 15 and 20 February, Iran increased its oil exports to 3 times normal rate, and reduced oil storage.[^164]

Just before the strikes began, on 27 February 2026, Oman's Foreign Minister [Badr Al-Busaidi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Badr_Al-Busaidi "Badr Al-Busaidi") said a "breakthrough" had been reached and Iran had agreed both to never stockpile enriched uranium and to full verification by the [International Atomic Energy Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency "International Atomic Energy Agency") (IAEA);[^165] furthermore, Iran had agreed to irreversibly downgrade its current enriched uranium to "the lowest level possible". Al-Busaidi said peace was "within reach".[^166] [^165] However, US Middle East envoy [Steve Witkoff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_Witkoff "Steve Witkoff") said Iran began recent nuclear talks by insisting on its "inalienable right" to [enrich uranium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enriched_uranium "Enriched uranium"), rejecting a US proposal for zero enrichment, and even boasting that its 460 kilograms of 60% enriched uranium could produce 11 nuclear bombs.[^167] [^168]

### US military buildup

A day later, on 14 February, US officials told [Reuters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reuters "Reuters") that the US military was preparing for a broad campaign involving weeks-long, sustained operations against Iran that could target its state and security infrastructure.[^169] By 19 February the [US buildup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_United_States_military_buildup_in_the_Middle_East "2026 United States military buildup in the Middle East") was described as the largest in the Middle East since the [2003 invasion of Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq "2003 invasion of Iraq").[^170] On 24 February 2026, during [a State of the Union speech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_State_of_the_Union_Address "2026 State of the Union Address"), Trump accused Iran of reviving efforts to build nuclear weapons, condemning these alleged ambitions as "sinister" and claiming that Iran had also developed increasingly advanced missile capabilities that could threaten the US, Europe, and US bases overseas. He warned that the US was prepared to act if necessary.[^171] Such claims by American officials have suggested that Iran is pursuing [weapons of mass destruction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction "Iran and weapons of mass destruction") (WMDs) or similar weapons and that the United States needed to intervene militarily against it, echoing false allegations of [WMDs in Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WMDs_in_Iraq "WMDs in Iraq") prior to the [Iraq War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq_War "Iraq War") in 2003.[^172] American intelligence reports suggested that alleged threats of long-range Iranian ballistic missiles were unfounded, with such capabilities requiring up until 2035 should Iran have decided to pursue the project.[^173]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Abraham_Lincoln_Carrier_Strike_Group_Conducts_Photo_Exercise.jpg/250px-Abraham_Lincoln_Carrier_Strike_Group_Conducts_Photo_Exercise.jpg)

Carrier Strike Group 3 sails in formation in the Arabian Sea during the 2026 United States military buildup in the Middle East, 6 February 2026

On 25 February 2026, Iranian Foreign Minister [Abbas Araghchi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbas_Araghchi "Abbas Araghchi") stated that a "historic" agreement with the United States to avert military conflict was "within reach" ahead of renewed talks in Geneva. Araghchi emphasized that diplomacy must be prioritized to avoid further escalation. Despite high tensions and a significant US military buildup in the region, Araghchi reiterated on social media that Iran holds a "crystal clear" position against developing nuclear weapons, while defending its right to peaceful nuclear technology.[^174]

Before the attack, [JD Vance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JD_Vance "JD Vance"), the [vice president of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vice_president_of_the_United_States "Vice president of the United States"), defended striking Iran. When asked about whether he would support a regime change in Iran despite previously criticizing the Iraq war, he said that life "has all kinds of crazy twists and turns".[^175] Vance has also supported the war after it began, contradicting his long-standing anti-war campaign.[^176] According to *[The Telegraph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph "The Daily Telegraph")* and *[The Washington Post](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Washington_Post "The Washington Post")*, crown prince of Saudi Arabia [Mohammed bin Salman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Salman "Mohammed bin Salman") conducted multiple phone calls with Trump urging him to attack Iran, stating that "Iran would become stronger and more dangerous if Washington did not strike immediately".[^177] *The Washington Post* reported that Trump's decision to attack Iran came after the [Saudi Arabian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia_lobby_in_the_United_States "Saudi Arabia lobby in the United States") and [Israeli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_lobby_in_the_United_States "Israel lobby in the United States") governments lobbied him repeatedly to make the move.[^92]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Marco_Rubio_visits_Israel_from_February_15_to_17%2C_2025_-_18.jpg/250px-Marco_Rubio_visits_Israel_from_February_15_to_17%2C_2025_-_18.jpg)

Israeli prime minister [Benjamin Netanyahu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu "Benjamin Netanyahu") successfully lobbied the Trump administration for military intervention.

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Donald_Trump_state_visit_to_Saudi_Arabia%2C_2025-05-13_P20250513DT-1367_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Donald_Trump_state_visit_to_Saudi_Arabia%2C_2025-05-13_P20250513DT-1367_%28cropped%29.jpg)

Saudi crown prince [Mohammed bin Salman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Salman "Mohammed bin Salman") reportedly urged Trump to strike Iran despite public calls for diplomacy.

*[The Guardian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guardian "The Guardian")* reported a few days before the attack that the decision would be determined by the outcome of a meeting in [Geneva](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geneva "Geneva"), in which the US would be led by Steve Witkoff and [Jared Kushner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jared_Kushner "Jared Kushner"). [Charles Wald](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Wald "Charles Wald"), a retired Air Force general and deputy commander of [US European Command](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US_European_Command "US European Command") who now serves at the [Jewish Institute for National Security of America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_Institute_for_National_Security_of_America "Jewish Institute for National Security of America"), stated that bringing the [*Gerald R. Ford* -class aircraft carrier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerald_R._Ford-class_aircraft_carrier "Gerald R. Ford-class aircraft carrier") to the Middle East would help defend Israel from Iran. He also stated that if US-Iran negotiations do not end well, that "it's going to be twice as bad as when Obama didn't do anything in Syria for the chemical weapons." [^178] However, according to [Royal United Services Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_United_Services_Institute "Royal United Services Institute"), there was no evidence of an imminent attack by Iran.[^179]

On the morning of the attack, some of Iran's top military and intelligence leaders, including Khamenei, were gathered together in the national security council offices for meetings. According to the *[Wall Street Journal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wall_Street_Journal "Wall Street Journal")*, Israeli and US military intelligence officers identified that the senior Iranian leaders would gather at three meetings that could be simultaneously struck. A *[New York Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Times "New York Times")* analysis stated that this was a mistake. It is still unknown how US and Israeli leadership were aware of their exact location.[^180] [^181] [^182]

A few days before the attack, senior advisors for the Trump administration said it would be better if Israel strikes Iran first, so that the United States would have a better justification for going to war after Iran retaliates.[^183] US secretary of state [Marco Rubio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marco_Rubio "Marco Rubio") later disclosed that the initial US attack on Iran was due to an Israeli intention to attack Iranian leadership, which would have jeopardized US forces in the region.[^184] He also stated that Israel dragged the United States into the war;[^185] however, Trump disagreed.[^186]

## Hostilities

### 28 February

#### Initial Israeli and American strikes

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/President_Donald_J._Trump_oversees_Operation_Epic_Fury_at_Mar-a-Lago%2C_Palm_Beach%2C_FL%2C_Feb._28%2C_2026._%28White_House_photo_by_Daniel_Torok%29_%2855121599389%29.jpg/250px-President_Donald_J._Trump_oversees_Operation_Epic_Fury_at_Mar-a-Lago%2C_Palm_Beach%2C_FL%2C_Feb._28%2C_2026._%28White_House_photo_by_Daniel_Torok%29_%2855121599389%29.jpg)

Trump and members of his cabinet oversee the strikes on Iran from the Mar-a-Lago resort in Palm Beach, Florida, on 28 February. 28

On 27 February, at 3:38 p.m. [EST](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone#Eastern_Standard_Time "Eastern Time Zone") (11:08 p.m. [IRST](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_Standard_Time "Iran Standard Time")) Donald Trump, travelling on [Air Force One](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_Force_One "Air Force One") to [Corpus Christi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corpus_Christi,_Texas "Corpus Christi, Texas"), Texas, gave the order to proceed with Operation Epic Fury.[^180] Airstrikes on Iran began on 28 February, Saturday, at around 9:45 a.m. IRST (1:15 a.m. EST); Saturday is the first day of the week in Iran and a regular work day.[^187] US missiles, drones, and [Israeli fighter jets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force#Current_inventory "Israeli Air Force") were used in the strikes.[^188] [Low-cost one-way attack drones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Low-cost_Uncrewed_Combat_Attack_System "Low-cost Uncrewed Combat Attack System") of Task Force Scorpion Strike were employed for the first time in combat.[^189]

Among the targets was the [Pasteur Street](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pasteur_Street "Pasteur Street") district in Tehran where Ali Khamenei normally resided; also home to the presidential palace and [National Security Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_National_Security_Council "Supreme National Security Council").[^190] Early reports suggested that at least seven missiles had struck the area.[^191] American officials confirmed that the strikes were coordinated with the US.[^192] The [Israeli Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force "Israeli Air Force") (IAF) said that it had struck 500 military targets in western and central Iran, including air defences and missile launchers, using approximately 200 fighter jets, in the largest combat sortie in its history.[^193]

Together with the physical airstrikes, Israel also conducted coordinated cyberattacks on Iranian infrastructure, media, and phone apps with messages calling on Iranians to rise up against their government.[^182] The popular BadeSaba Calendar prayer app (over 5 million downloads) was also compromised in the attack; it was hacked early that morning to broadcast push notifications in Persian urging military personnel and citizens to defect, lay down weapons, and join opposition forces with messages such as "Help has arrived" and "It's time for reckoning." [^194] [^195] [^196] The cyberattacks resulted in a near-total internet blackout in Iran, lasting over 60 hours with connectivity dropping to as low as 1–4% of normal levels, disrupting government communications, state media, and public services.[^197] [^195]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Attack_on_Sanandaj_Residential_Areas_1.jpg/250px-Attack_on_Sanandaj_Residential_Areas_1.jpg)

Damage to residential buildings in Sanandaj, Iranian Kurdistan, following a military strike

Israel subsequently declared a [state of emergency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Israeli_state_of_emergency "2026 Israeli state of emergency"), citing expectation of an Iranian attack.[^198] Sirens blared in Israel as the government warned its citizens to remain in protected areas.[^199] Trump warned that US lives may be lost.[^200] The [Israeli Ministry of Health](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Ministry_of_Health "Israeli Ministry of Health") moved its hospital operations underground.[^201] According to [Iran International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_International "Iran International"), Israel warned Iranian civilians residing near military industries and infrastructure to evacuate immediately, stating "Your presence in these areas puts your life at risk." [^202]

According to a US official, dozens of US strikes were carried out by planes based around the Middle East and from one or more aircraft carriers.[^203] Israeli military officials said months-long planning preceded their strikes, allowing them to pinpoint their targets, attain "tactical surprise", and gain US support.[^204] Attacking during the morning, rather than at night which was when most of Israel's previous attacks on Iran took place, added to the element of surprise. Israeli weapons included the newly developed [Black Sparrow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sparrow_\(target_missile\) "Sparrow (target missile)") air-launched ballistic missile, fired from F-15s.[^181] Israel later stated its initial strikes used over 1,200 bombs in 24 hours.[^205] Iranian naval vessels were also targeted.[^206]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Attack_on_Lamerd_1_Tasnim_28Feb2026.jpg/250px-Attack_on_Lamerd_1_Tasnim_28Feb2026.jpg)

Damaged residential area in Lamerd, southwest Iran, following a reported missile attack targeting local infrastructure

A sports hall in [Lamerd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lamerd "Lamerd") was bombed during a girls' practice, killing at least 18 civilians.[^207] Communication services across Tehran were impaired following the attacks,[^48] and a near total internet blackout was reported by [Netblocks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netblocks "Netblocks").[^208] [^209] [^210] According to the BBC, Khamenei's office and the presidential office of [Masoud Pezeshkian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masoud_Pezeshkian "Masoud Pezeshkian") in Tehran were hit during the strikes.[^208] Reuters quoted an unnamed Israeli official who stated that Khamenei's body had been found, confirming death.[^211]

A spokesperson for the Iraqi [Popular Mobilization Forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_Mobilization_Forces "Popular Mobilization Forces") said that two of its fighters had been killed while three more had been injured during strikes in [Jurf al-Sakhar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jurf_al-Sakhar "Jurf al-Sakhar"), south of [Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad "Baghdad").[^48] According to Iran International, quoting the [Iranian Students' News Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Students%27_News_Agency "Iranian Students' News Agency"), thousands of [IRGC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Revolutionary_Guard_Corps "Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps") personnel, including several senior officials,[^212] were killed or wounded as several military bases were attacked.[^202] It reported that the port city of [Bushehr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bushehr "Bushehr") had also been struck; however, it was unclear whether the [nuclear reactor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bushehr_Nuclear_Power_Plant "Bushehr Nuclear Power Plant") had sustained any damage.[^202] Rafael Mariano Grossi, the U.N. nuclear watchdog chief stated that no evidence has been found that nuclear facilities [^213] have been hit from these attacks.[^214]

Israel called up 20,000 in addition to the 50,000 reservists who are on duty.[^215] On 2 March 2026, Khamenei's wife [Mansoureh Khojasteh Bagherzadeh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mansoureh_Khojasteh_Bagherzadeh "Mansoureh Khojasteh Bagherzadeh") was confirmed to have also died of injuries sustained in the strike.[^216]

#### Israeli and American leaders' statements on their aims
