kind="subtitles" type="text/vtt" srclang="zh-Hant" label="中文（繁體） ‪(zh-hant)‬"></video>

Trump addresses the nation regarding the strikes, 28 February 2026

At exactly 2:30 AM EST on 28 February, Donald Trump released an eight-minute video statement on Truth Social, saying that the purpose of the US strikes in Iran was effectively regime change. Trump said that Iran's "menacing activities" endangered the US and its allies. He cited the [Iran hostage crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_hostage_crisis "Iran hostage crisis"), support for proxies such as Hamas and Hezbollah, its killings of protesters, and its alleged pursuit of nuclear weapons. He asserted that in the conflict, "The lives of courageous American heroes may be lost and we may have casualties. That often happens in war".[^217]

Trump urged members of the IRGC to "lay down your weapons and have complete [immunity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immunity_from_prosecution_\(international_law\) "Immunity from prosecution (international law)"), or in the alternative, face certain death". Calling on the Iranian public to initiate regime change,[^218] he said: "When we are finished, take over your government. It will be yours to take. This will be probably your only chance for generations." [^87] [^107] [^219]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Vice_President_JD_Vance_meets_with_members_of_the_Cabinet_in_the_Situation_Room_at_the_White_House_%2855127462186%29.jpg/250px-Vice_President_JD_Vance_meets_with_members_of_the_Cabinet_in_the_Situation_Room_at_the_White_House_%2855127462186%29.jpg)

Vice President JD Vance with cabinet members in the Situation Room during the strikes.

Shortly after, [Benjamin Netanyahu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu "Benjamin Netanyahu") released a video statement saying Israel and the United States had launched strikes against Iran "to remove the existential threat" posed by what he called "the terror regime in Iran". Netanyahu accused Iran's leadership of decades of hostility, saying that "for 47 years, the Ayatollah regime has called out ' [Death to Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_to_Israel "Death to Israel") ' and ' [Death to America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_to_America "Death to America") ' ", and described it as a "murderous terror regime" that "must not be allowed to arm itself with nuclear weapons". He said the joint US-Israeli action would "create the conditions for the brave Iranian people to take their destiny into their own hands", and called on the people of Iran to "cast off the yoke of tyranny".[^220] *[The Times of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Times_of_Israel "The Times of Israel")* reported that [Israeli Defense Minister](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Defense_\(Israel\) "Ministry of Defense (Israel)") [Israel Katz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_Katz "Israel Katz") had labelled the strikes a "pre-emptive attack" intended to "remove threats to the State of Israel".[^198]

[United States secretary of defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_secretary_of_defense "United States secretary of defense") [Pete Hegseth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pete_Hegseth "Pete Hegseth") dismissed concerns raised by some Democrats in the US, saying "No stupid rules of engagement, no nation building quagmire, no democracy building exercise, no politically correct wars. We fight to win and we don't waste time or lives. As the president warned, an effort of this scope will include casualties. War is hell and always will be." [^221] Iran rejected claims that it intended to attack the United States, citing the aggressive posture of the US armed forces as evidence.[^108]

#### Iranian response and missile attacks in the Persian Gulf theatre

Iranian forces reacted within hours by launching missiles against targets in [Tel Aviv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv "Tel Aviv") and [Haifa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haifa "Haifa") as well as the US military bases in the [Persian Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf "Persian Gulf") region. The quicker response relative to that of the [Twelve-Day War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twelve-Day_War "Twelve-Day War") suggests a change in Iran's command structure, according to the BBC.[^222]

Iran targeted multiple US military bases throughout the Persian Gulf region.[^223] [Bahrain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bahrain "Bahrain") activated air-raid sirens to warn of an Iranian attack on US military bases within the nation, with Arabic media saying explosions and smoke were seen in the capital, [Manama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manama "Manama").[^224] [^225] Bahrain later confirmed the strikes and said that the US [Fifth Fleet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fifth_Fleet "Fifth Fleet") headquarters had been targeted.[^226] Explosions were also reported at [Kuwait International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_International_Airport "Kuwait International Airport") and [Abu Dhabi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abu_Dhabi "Abu Dhabi") in the [United Arab Emirates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates "United Arab Emirates").[^227] [^228] Following the missile and drone attacks on Kuwait, its Foreign Ministry summoned Mohammad Toutounchi, Iran's ambassador in Kuwait.[^229]

The IRGC said that Iran had targeted four US bases in the Middle East: [Al Udeid Air Base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Udeid_Air_Base "Al Udeid Air Base") in Qatar, [Ali Al Salem Air Base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Al_Salem_Air_Base "Ali Al Salem Air Base") in Kuwait (which also hosted Italian soldiers),[^230] [Al Dhafra Air Base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Dhafra_Air_Base "Al Dhafra Air Base") in the UAE, and the US Navy Fifth Fleet headquarters in Bahrain, and a video was posted in which smoke could be seen rising from the direction of the base in Bahrain.[^231] Saudi Arabia confirmed that there had been Iranian attacks on [Riyadh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Riyadh "Riyadh") and its [Eastern Province](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Province,_Saudi_Arabia "Eastern Province, Saudi Arabia").[^232] It claimed to have successfully intercepted Iranian attacks aimed at those areas and said that the Kingdom will "take all necessary measures" to defend itself, "including the option of responding to aggression".[^233]

The UAE stated that it had successfully intercepted a number of Iranian missiles and that one Asian national had been killed by interceptor debris which had fallen on a residential area.[^208] [^234] Qatar said that it had intercepted at least two waves of missile attacks, stating that no casualties or property damage had been reported.[^235] In the [Kurdistan Region of Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdistan_Region_of_Iraq "Kurdistan Region of Iraq"), Iranian aerial attacks targeted infrastructure hosting US military and civilian personnel, including [Erbil International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erbil_International_Airport "Erbil International Airport") and the [US Consulate General in Erbil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consulate_General_of_the_United_States_in_Erbil "Consulate General of the United States in Erbil"). However, according to local media reports, most missiles and drones had been intercepted.[^236]

A nine-storey building was hit by missiles in northern Israel, injuring one person.[^48] Strikes were reported in [Haifa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haifa "Haifa") and [Tel Aviv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv "Tel Aviv").[^237] A strike on a residential area in Tel Aviv killed a civilian woman in her 40s and injured 27 others.[^238] Reports claim missiles from Iran had hit [Jordanian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan "Jordan") territories and the capital [Amman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amman "Amman").[^239] [^240] Jordan said that its armed forces had shot down two Iranian ballistic missiles targeting its territory [^208] and that it had handled 54 reports of falling debris that caused material damage but no casualties.[^241] Residential areas of [Dubai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dubai "Dubai") in the proximity of the [Burj Khalifa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burj_Khalifa "Burj Khalifa"), [Dubai Marina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dubai_Marina "Dubai Marina") and the [Dubai Palm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palm_Islands "Palm Islands") were hit by strikes, setting the [Fairmont The Palm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fairmont_The_Palm "Fairmont The Palm") hotel on fire,[^242] causing four injuries,[^48] as well as a residential building on the outskirts of Doha.[^243] [^235] [^244] [^245] Local sources say Iran used [Shahed drones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shahed_drones "Shahed drones"), which are among the weapons most used by Iran and its proxies, including Hamas and Hezbollah.[^246]

The UAE said that it had intercepted a "new wave" of Iranian missiles and that "fragments from the interceptions" had fallen in Abu Dhabi and Dubai, causing damage to [Burj Al Arab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burj_Al_Arab "Burj Al Arab").[^247] [^248] Strikes on Kuwait International Airport caused several undefined injuries.[^242] In Bahrain during the evening a tower in a residential area was reported to be hit by an Iranian drone.[^48] According to an analysis in Reuters, by sending missiles at Gulf states, Iran has caused the Gulf states to realize that Iran poses a threat to them, and could thus cause them to support the US-Israel strikes.[^249] Former CIA Director [David Petraeus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Petraeus "David Petraeus") echoed these sentiments, stating that Iran's targeting of other Gulf states was likely a strategic error that could pull additional countries into the war.[^250]

### 1 March

      <video controls="" width="201" height="106"><source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/2e/Operation_Epic_Fury_Update%2C_President_Donald_J._Trump.webm/Operation_Epic_Fury_Update%2C_President_Donald_J._Trump.webm.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/2e/Operation_Epic_Fury_Update%2C_President_Donald_J._Trump.webm/Operation_Epic_Fury_Update%2C_President_Donald_J._Trump.webm.1080p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2e/Operation_Epic_Fury_Update%2C_President_Donald_J._Trump.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;av01.0.12M.08, opus&quot;"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/2e/Operation_Epic_Fury_Update%2C_President_Donald_J._Trump.webm/Operation_Epic_Fury_Update%2C_President_Donald_J._Trump.webm.144p.mjpeg.mov" type="video/quicktime"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/2e/Operation_Epic_Fury_Update%2C_President_Donald_J._Trump.webm/Operation_Epic_Fury_Update%2C_President_Donald_J._Trump.webm.240p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/2e/Operation_Epic_Fury_Update%2C_President_Donald_J._Trump.webm/Operation_Epic_Fury_Update%2C_President_Donald_J._Trump.webm.360p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp8, vorbis&quot;"> <track src="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3AOperation_Epic_Fury_Update%2C_President_Donald_J._Trump.webm&amp;lang=en&amp;trackformat=vtt&amp;origin=%2A" kind="subtitles" type="text/vtt" srclang="en" label="English ‪(en)‬"></video>

President Trump delivers an update on the strikes, including the assassination of Ali Khamenei.

Iran's top security official, [Ali Larijani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Larijani "Ali Larijani"), announced the [Interim Leadership Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interim_Leadership_Council "Interim Leadership Council") on 1 March and accused the US and Israel of trying to dismantle Iran. He warned "secessionist groups" of severe consequences if they take action.[^251] Trump relayed to [NBC News](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC_News "NBC News") that "a large amount of leadership" in Iran had been killed.[^252] Israel launches a new wave of strikes against Iranian targets.[^251]

Iran launched missiles and drones on Israel, UAE, Qatar, Kuwait, Bahrain, Jordan, and Saudi Arabia.[^253] [^254] [^255] The United Kingdom initially reported there were strikes against Cyprus,[^256] [^257] but later confirmed that there were not.[^258] Two oil tankers, the [Palau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palau "Palau") -flagged *Skylight* and the [Marshall Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marshall_Islands "Marshall Islands") -flagged *MKD VYOM*, were targeted off the coast of Oman.[^259] [^260] [^261] As a result of the war and higher risk to ships, 150 freight ships, including many oil tankers, are stalled behind the strait.[^262]

To avert further Iranian strikes, the [E3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EU_three#E3 "EU three") (the UK, France, and Germany) resolved to back, if needed, "proportionate military defensive measures" against drones and ballistic missiles, signaling the potential for direct involvement.[^263] British prime minister Keir Starmer said that US can use British bases for "defensive" strikes on Iran [^264] and disclosed that Ukrainian and other specialists would aid Gulf efforts to foil Iranian drone strikes.[^265] [CNN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CNN "CNN") reported that Crown Prince Salman, with US backing, vowed to employ military force against further Iranian incursions, calling Iranian strikes "cowardly" due to Saudi airspace being closed to US and Israeli attackers.[^266] On 1 March, Trump announced that the US had accepted an Iranian proposal to further negotiations.[^267] Trump later said the US operations were to be completed within a four-week timetable in an interview with the *[Daily Mail](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daily_Mail "Daily Mail")*.[^268] However, Ali Larijani subsequently ruled out talks.[^269]

### 2 March

     <video controls="" width="201" height="113"><source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/4/4f/Epic_Fury_Strike_compilation_%28997855%29.webm/Epic_Fury_Strike_compilation_%28997855%29.webm.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/4/4f/Epic_Fury_Strike_compilation_%28997855%29.webm/Epic_Fury_Strike_compilation_%28997855%29.webm.1080p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4f/Epic_Fury_Strike_compilation_%28997855%29.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;av01.0.08M.08, opus&quot;"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/4/4f/Epic_Fury_Strike_compilation_%28997855%29.webm/Epic_Fury_Strike_compilation_%28997855%29.webm.144p.mjpeg.mov" type="video/quicktime"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/4/4f/Epic_Fury_Strike_compilation_%28997855%29.webm/Epic_Fury_Strike_compilation_%28997855%29.webm.240p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/4/4f/Epic_Fury_Strike_compilation_%28997855%29.webm/Epic_Fury_Strike_compilation_%28997855%29.webm.360p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp8, vorbis&quot;"></video>

A montage of US Central Command strikes during Operation Epic Fury in Iran, 2 March 2026

      <video controls="" width="201" height="113"><source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c3/Message_from_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Cyprus%2C_Mr._Nikos_Christodoulides_following_first_Iranian_strikes_on_Cyprus.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/c/c3/Message_from_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Cyprus%2C_Mr._Nikos_Christodoulides_following_first_Iranian_strikes_on_Cyprus.webm/Message_from_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Cyprus%2C_Mr._Nikos_Christodoulides_following_first_Iranian_strikes_on_Cyprus.webm.360p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp8, vorbis&quot;"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/c/c3/Message_from_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Cyprus%2C_Mr._Nikos_Christodoulides_following_first_Iranian_strikes_on_Cyprus.webm/Message_from_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Cyprus%2C_Mr._Nikos_Christodoulides_following_first_Iranian_strikes_on_Cyprus.webm.144p.mjpeg.mov" type="video/quicktime"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/c/c3/Message_from_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Cyprus%2C_Mr._Nikos_Christodoulides_following_first_Iranian_strikes_on_Cyprus.webm/Message_from_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Cyprus%2C_Mr._Nikos_Christodoulides_following_first_Iranian_strikes_on_Cyprus.webm.240p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;"> <track src="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3AMessage_from_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Cyprus%2C_Mr._Nikos_Christodoulides_following_first_Iranian_strikes_on_Cyprus.webm&amp;lang=el&amp;trackformat=vtt&amp;origin=%2A" kind="subtitles" type="text/vtt" srclang="el" label="Ελληνικά ‪(el)‬"> <track src="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3AMessage_from_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Cyprus%2C_Mr._Nikos_Christodoulides_following_first_Iranian_strikes_on_Cyprus.webm&amp;lang=en&amp;trackformat=vtt&amp;origin=%2A" kind="subtitles" type="text/vtt" srclang="en" label="English ‪(en)‬"> <track src="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3AMessage_from_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Cyprus%2C_Mr._Nikos_Christodoulides_following_first_Iranian_strikes_on_Cyprus.webm&amp;lang=ro&amp;trackformat=vtt&amp;origin=%2A" kind="subtitles" type="text/vtt" srclang="ro" label="română ‪(ro)‬"></video>

Message (in Greek) from President of Cyprus, Nikos Christodoulides, following the first Iranian strikes on Cyprus on 2 March 2026

Iranian strikes were reported on 2 March, including in Dubai, Abu Dhabi, Doha,[^59] and [Beersheba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beersheba "Beersheba").[^270] The [US embassy in Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US_embassy_in_Kuwait "US embassy in Kuwait") was struck and subsequently closed indefinitely.[^271] [^272] The US-flagged tanker *Stena Imperative* and the Honduras-flagged tanker *Athe Nova* were also struck.[^273] [^273] A senior IRGC official who is an advisor to the IRGC commander said he would set fire onto any ship coming through the Strait of Hormuz, and added that no oil will leave the area.[^274] Qatar shot down two [Iranian Su-24 bombers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-24 "Sukhoi Su-24"), making it the first nation to shoot down an Iranian aircraft in the conflict.[^59]

Israel and the United States attacked the [Natanz Nuclear Facility](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natanz_Nuclear_Facility "Natanz Nuclear Facility") [^275] and the Khatam-al-Anbia and Gandhi hospitals.[^276] A double tap strike on Tehran's Niloofar Square killed more than 20 civilians.[^277] A [friendly fire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friendly_fire "Friendly fire") incident took place when an [Kuwait Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Air_Force "Kuwait Air Force") [F/A-18](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/F/A-18 "F/A-18") pilot shot down three US F-15 fighters.[^278] [^279] [^280] [^272] According to Saudi-owned *[Al Arabiya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Arabiya "Al Arabiya")*, in the evening, Israeli special forces and Mossad operatives carried out a ground operation inside Iran; no additional information was reported. Israeli authorities did not issue a response to the report by 3 March. No independent news outlet has confirmed these allegations.[^281]

Israel and Hezbollah exchanged strikes against one another.[^282] Hezbollah launched attacks against Israel in retaliation for Khamenei's killing.[^100] Lebanon banned military activities by Hezbollah after the attacks.[^283] Hezbollah later claimed that the attack was a "defensive act" after over a year of Israeli attacks despite a truce.[^101] It added that it restarted fighting to force Israel to stop its aggression and evacuate from seized Lebanese territories, emphasising that the move was unrelated to the war.[^102] An IDF spokesperson issued an emergency statement stating that the attack is to be considered "an official declaration of war by Hezbollah", vowing to "neutralize" the threat.[^282] Israel struck [southern Lebanon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Lebanon "Southern Lebanon"),[^284] [^285] [^286] Beirut, and the [Beqaa Valley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beqaa_Valley "Beqaa Valley").[^282] The IDF said it killed the head of Hezbollah's intelligence headquarters [Hussein Makled](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hussein_Makled&action=edit&redlink=1 "Hussein Makled (page does not exist)") in the strikes.[^287] [^288]

The Royal Air Force station at [Akrotiri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RAF_Akrotiri "RAF Akrotiri"), Cyprus, was targeted by a drone strike around midnight local time, with one causing minor damage.[^289] [^290] [^291] [^292] Another strike on Cyprus led to [Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greece "Greece") announcing that they would deploy frigates and [F-16s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/F-16 "F-16") to defend Cyprus from any further strikes by Iran.[^293] Later in the day IRGC general [Sardar Jabbari](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sardar_Jabbari&action=edit&redlink=1 "Sardar Jabbari (page does not exist)") commented that there was a US presence on the island of Cyprus and that Iran planned to strike the island "with such intensity that the Americans will be forced to leave".[^294] [^295] The pro-Iran militant group [Guardians of the Blood Brigade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraqi_Guardians_of_Blood_Brigades "Iraqi Guardians of Blood Brigades") claimed responsibility for attacks on the US [Victory Base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victory_Base_Complex "Victory Base Complex") near [Baghdad International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad_International_Airport "Baghdad International Airport") and [Erbil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erbil "Erbil"), [Kurdistan Region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdistan_Region "Kurdistan Region"), Iraq.[^285] [^296] [^297] The [Islamic Resistance in Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Resistance_in_Iraq "Islamic Resistance in Iraq") claimed responsibility for over 23 drone strikes on US assets in Erbil.[^298]

### 3 March

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Attack_around_Enghelab_Square_9.jpg/250px-Attack_around_Enghelab_Square_9.jpg)

Enghelab Square, Tehran, 3 March 2026

On 3 March, Israeli and US strikes reportedly destroyed the [Supreme National Security Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_National_Security_Council "Supreme National Security Council") (SNSC) headquarters,[^299] the [Expediency Discernment Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expediency_Discernment_Council "Expediency Discernment Council") building in Tehran,[^300] and what Israeli officials described as an underground nuclear weapons facility called Min Zadai.[^301] [Bushehr Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bushehr_Airport "Bushehr Airport") was also struck, damaging the airport terminal and destroying an [Iran Air](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_Air "Iran Air") [Airbus A319](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airbus_A319 "Airbus A319") (EP-IEP).[^302] [^303] The proximity of these strikes to the [Bushehr Nuclear Power Plant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bushehr_Nuclear_Power_Plant "Bushehr Nuclear Power Plant") (about 12 km (7.5 mi) away) prompted the Russian agency [Rosatom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rosatom "Rosatom") to suspend construction on new units and evacuate non-essential staff due to a loss of communication with Iranian officials.[^304]

US officials said US forces severely damaged Iran's naval capabilities, mainly in the Gulf of Oman, where several Iranian warships have reportedly been destroyed and key bases hit.[^305] [^306] Israel also reported that it killed [Daoud Alizadeh](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Daoud_Alizadeh&action=edit&redlink=1 "Daoud Alizadeh (page does not exist)"), the commander of the Quds Force's Lebanon branch, in Tehran,[^307] and that it detained a dozen Hezbollah members in response to a missile strike.[^71] Debris from an Israeli-US airstrike damaged [Golestan Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golestan_Palace "Golestan Palace"), a [UNESCO World Heritage Site](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site "UNESCO World Heritage Site"),[^308] causing UNESCO to issue a statement that damaging UNESCO property is against international law.[^309]

Israel Katz [authorized a ground invasion of Lebanon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Hezbollah%E2%80%93Israel_strikes "2026 Hezbollah–Israel strikes") on 3 March.[^310] [^311] Israeli officials warned its attacks against Iran could become more intense and involve a deeper ground invasion.[^312] The US expressed reluctance to deploy its own ground troops to Iran.[^313] Trump said the US retained a "virtually unlimited supply" of heavy weaponry, but that it was seeking more supplies from other states. Trump added that he was confident in a "BIG" US victory.[^314]

Earlier in the conflict, Trump urged Iranians to "take over your government" and said that "America is backing you with overwhelming strength and devastating force", framing US military action as an opportunity for a broader uprising. Trump also reshared opinion pieces arguing that "there is no need for a U.S. invasion force...the Iranian people are the boots on the ground", signaling support for internal resistance.[^315] However, the day before, US defense secretary Pete Hegseth said he would not rule out sending American ground troops to Iran.[^316]

Western diplomats and other sources told *[The Jerusalem Post](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Jerusalem_Post "The Jerusalem Post")* that Qatar had struck Iran after Iran had attempted to strike Doha's airport and Qatar shot down two Iranian [Su-24](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-24 "Sukhoi Su-24") bombers;[^313] [Channel 12](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Channel_12_\(Israel\) "Channel 12 (Israel)") also reported Qatari strikes.[^317] Qatari Foreign Ministry spokesperson [Majed al-Ansari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Majed_al-Ansari "Majed al-Ansari") vigorously denied the accusation that Qatar had joined the "campaign targeting Iran".[^40]

Iran continued retaliating with strikes on Israel and the Gulf states.[^318] [^319] [^320] Iranian general of the IRGC warned it would hit all economic hubs in the Middle East,[^321] [^322] and Abbas Araghchi said that any defensive European military involvement would be considered an act of war.[^323] [^324] Hezbollah launched drones and missiles at a trio of Israeli bases,[^325] [^326] and the Islamic Resistance in Iraq claimed responsibility for explosions in Erbil.[^327]

#### Kurdish militias

According to *[The Wall Street Journal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal "The Wall Street Journal")*, Trump was open to supporting armed militias, particularly [Kurds in Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurds_in_Iran "Kurds in Iran") that have been [in conflict with Tehran for decades](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdish_separatism_in_Iran "Kurdish separatism in Iran").[^313] *[The Washington Post](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Washington_Post "The Washington Post")* reported that Trump had called Kurdish minority leaders, offering [air support](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Close_air_support "Close air support") and military backing for the [Kurds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurds "Kurds") to take over parts of [Western Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Iran "Western Iran").[^328] The [Kurds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurds "Kurds") have historically been a regional ally of the United States.[^329] The reports coincided with intensified strikes in the Kurdish-majority areas of western Iran ([Iranian Kurdistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Kurdistan "Iranian Kurdistan")) targeting police stations, border posts along the [Iran–Iraq border](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_border "Iran–Iraq border"), and other security facilities, which some sources suggested may have "paved the way for a Kurdish advance" [^313] [^330] [^331] [^332] and also hinted at a strategy built around the Kurds.[^333] The human rights organization [Hengaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hengaw "Hengaw") stated that the strikes had already resulted in the deaths of hundreds of Iranian security personnel in the Kurdish regions, which it said may have been "underreported".[^334] A few days after the start of the attacks, Trump also held calls with Kurdish leaders of the [Kurdistan Region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdistan_Region "Kurdistan Region") of Iraq's two main parties, [Masoud Barzani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masoud_Barzani "Masoud Barzani") and [Bafel Talabani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bafel_Talabani "Bafel Talabani"), discussing what were described as "sensitive" topics.[^335]

The Kurdistan Region hosts several armed Iranian Kurdish opposition groups, which have declared their readiness to help topple the Iranian regime under the umbrella of the [Coalition of Political Forces of Iranian Kurdistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coalition_of_Political_Forces_of_Iranian_Kurdistan "Coalition of Political Forces of Iranian Kurdistan") (CPFIK).[^336] [^337] These groups had already become targets of Iranian strikes during the conflict, with Iranian drones and missiles [hitting their bases and camps in the Kurdistan Region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iranian_strikes_on_the_Kurdistan_Region "2026 Iranian strikes on the Kurdistan Region"), and some also claimed to have carried out combat operations inside Iran.[^338]

According to [ITV News](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ITV_News "ITV News"), since the start of last year, weapons have been smuggled into western Iran to arm thousands of Kurdish volunteers, and Kurdish sources have told the outlet that US and Israeli forces were asked to provide air cover when any such ground operation begins.[^339] These reports were corroborated by CNN, which stated that the [CIA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CIA "CIA") was working to arm Kurdish forces to spark an uprising in Iran, and that President Trump had a phone call with [Mustafa Hijri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustafa_Hijri "Mustafa Hijri"), the leader of the [Democratic Party of Iranian Kurdistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Iranian_Kurdistan "Democratic Party of Iranian Kurdistan").[^329]

### 4 March

#### Israeli and US strikes

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Operation-Roaring-Lion-0011.jpg/250px-Operation-Roaring-Lion-0011.jpg)

An Israeli Air Force F-35I "Adir" shot down an Iranian YAK-130, scoring the first kill of manned aircraft by the F-35.

The IDF announced that an [F-35I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/F-35I "F-35I") "Adir" shot down a Russian-made Iranian [Yak-130](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yak-130 "Yak-130") fighter jet over Tehran, the first time that an F-35 has ever shot down a manned fighter jet in air-to-air combat. It was also the first time the Israeli Air Force shot down an aircraft since 1985.[^340] Rubio announced that the US-Israeli attacks on Iran are going to increase in their intensity.[^54] Israel attacks hit the [Basij](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basij "Basij") headquarters.[^341] According to Iranian sources [Mojtaba Khamenei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mojtaba_Khamenei "Mojtaba Khamenei") survived an airstrike.[^342]

#### Iranian retaliation and Hezbollah strikes

Qatar arrested ten individuals for operating as a cell of the IRGC in Qatari territory, collecting data on military infrastructure, with some trained to use drones.[^343] An 11 year-old Kuwaiti girl died from her injuries following an incident related to Iranian shrapnel.[^344] The [Al Udeid Air Base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Udeid_Air_Base "Al Udeid Air Base"), which has been described as "the largest American base in the Middle East" was hit with no casualties, reported the Qatari Ministry of Defense.[^345] Aramco's Ras Tanura oil refining facility was hit by a projectile.[^346]

[Larnaca International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larnaca_International_Airport "Larnaca International Airport") was temporarily closed due to the sighting of an unidentified object. It was later identified as a drone from Lebanon attempting to enter Cypriot airspace. It was shot down by Greek F-16s mobilized in the area following Iranian threats.[^347] [^348] Reports suggested a closure of Cypriot airspace, but it was later dismissed as false by the Cypriot government, which also confirmed the existence of the unidentified object from Lebanon in the same statement.[^349]

A ballistic missile was intercepted by NATO forces in [Turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey "Turkey") in [Dörtyol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D%C3%B6rtyol "Dörtyol"), [Hatay Province](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hatay_Province "Hatay Province"), with a statement following interception stating that Turkey reserved the right to defend its territory and that the ordnance had fallen in its territory.[^350] No casualties were reported by the statement. A senior U.S. military official said that it had been shot down by an [SM-3 interceptor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RIM-161_Standard_Missile_3 "RIM-161 Standard Missile 3") launched from [USS *Oscar Austin*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USS_Oscar_Austin "USS Oscar Austin").[^351] An anonymous Turkish official stated that the missile was directed towards "Greek Cyprus".[^352] The pro-Iran militia [Saraya Awliya al-Dam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saraya_Awliya_al-Dam "Saraya Awliya al-Dam") claimed that they struck a "vital US asset" in Jordan, but this has not been confirmed either by an independent news outlet or CENTCOM.[^353]

Hezbollah claimed that it struck an Israeli tank in the town of [Houla, Lebanon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houla,_Lebanon "Houla, Lebanon").[^354] Israel later said that two soldiers were injured by anti-tank fire in southern Lebanon.[^355] The rate of ballistic missile launches by Iran declined from the beginning of the war to 4 March, with analysts pointing to a depletion of Iranian missile and launcher stores as well as a strategy of rationing for a longer war as explanatory factors.[^356] On 5 March, [Lebanese Health Ministry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Public_Health_\(Lebanon\) "Ministry of Public Health (Lebanon)") said that those killed in Lebanon in the last 24 hours include seven children.[^357]

#### Political and safety developments in Cyprus

Non-essential American workers in [Cyprus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprus "Cyprus") were asked to evacuate Cyprus due to the risks of a possible Iranian incursion in the future.[^358] After, the US State Department stated to avoid travelling to Cyprus given the current crisis.[^359] In an emergency meeting in [Rome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rome "Rome"), [Giorgia Meloni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giorgia_Meloni "Giorgia Meloni") and other Italian officials considered sending reinforcement to Cyprus following the deployment by other European nations (Greece, France, Germany and the United Kingdom), specifically considering the deployment of the destroyer *[Caio Duilio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_destroyer_Caio_Duilio "Italian destroyer Caio Duilio")* as a possibility (with capability up to 350 kilometers).[^360]

#### Sinking of IRIS Dena and Sri Lankan rescue efforts

     <video controls="" width="200" height="113"><source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/f4/OSINTtechnical_-_Periscope_footage_of_a_US_Navy_Submarine_torpedoing_the_Iranian_Friga....webm/OSINTtechnical_-_Periscope_footage_of_a_US_Navy_Submarine_torpedoing_the_Iranian_Friga....webm.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f4/OSINTtechnical_-_Periscope_footage_of_a_US_Navy_Submarine_torpedoing_the_Iranian_Friga....webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;av01.0.08M.08&quot;"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/f4/OSINTtechnical_-_Periscope_footage_of_a_US_Navy_Submarine_torpedoing_the_Iranian_Friga....webm/OSINTtechnical_-_Periscope_footage_of_a_US_Navy_Submarine_torpedoing_the_Iranian_Friga....webm.1080p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/f4/OSINTtechnical_-_Periscope_footage_of_a_US_Navy_Submarine_torpedoing_the_Iranian_Friga....webm/OSINTtechnical_-_Periscope_footage_of_a_US_Navy_Submarine_torpedoing_the_Iranian_Friga....webm.144p.mjpeg.mov" type="video/quicktime"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/f4/OSINTtechnical_-_Periscope_footage_of_a_US_Navy_Submarine_torpedoing_the_Iranian_Friga....webm/OSINTtechnical_-_Periscope_footage_of_a_US_Navy_Submarine_torpedoing_the_Iranian_Friga....webm.240p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;"> <source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/f4/OSINTtechnical_-_Periscope_footage_of_a_US_Navy_Submarine_torpedoing_the_Iranian_Friga....webm/OSINTtechnical_-_Periscope_footage_of_a_US_Navy_Submarine_torpedoing_the_Iranian_Friga....webm.360p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp8, vorbis&quot;"></video>

Dena sinking after being torpedoed by a US submarine

On 4 March 2026, the Iranian Navy frigate [IRIS *Dena*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IRIS_Dena "IRIS Dena") was sunk in the Indian Ocean by [United States Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Navy "United States Navy") submarines, approximately 40 nautical miles (74 km; 46 mi) south of [Galle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galle "Galle"), Sri Lanka. The vessel was transiting back to Iran following its participation in the [International Fleet Review 2026](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Fleet_Review_2026 "International Fleet Review 2026") and the multilateral [Exercise MILAN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milan_\(naval_exercise\) "Milan (naval exercise)") at [Visakhapatnam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visakhapatnam "Visakhapatnam"), India.[^361] [^362] [^363] It was the first ship sunk by a submarine in active combat since [ARA *General Belgrano*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ARA_General_Belgrano "ARA General Belgrano") during the [Falklands War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Falklands_War "Falklands War"), and the first by an American submarine since [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II").[^29] [^366]

Preliminary reports and military sources suggest the frigate was targeted by a United States Navy submarine operating in the region as part of the broader escalation of hostilities between the US-Israeli coalition and Iran.[^367] [^368] The ship issued a distress signal at dawn, prompting an immediate search and rescue operation by the [Sri Lanka Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Navy "Sri Lanka Navy") and [Sri Lanka Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Air_Force "Sri Lanka Air Force").The [Indian Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Navy "Indian Navy") also diverted its assets in the region to conduct search and rescue efforts for the crew.[^369]

According to the [Sri Lankan Ministry of Defence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_\(Sri_Lanka\) "Ministry of Defence (Sri Lanka)"), the ship sank in the early morning before rescue forces had reached the area.[^341] Thirty-two crew members were rescued and transported to the [Karapitiya Teaching Hospital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galle_National_Hospital "Galle National Hospital") in Galle for treatment of blast-related injuries and exhaustion. However, over 100 personnel remain unaccounted for, with at least 78 reported wounded during the initial strike. Another Iranian vessel, [IRIS *Bushehr*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bandar_Abbas-class_replenishment_ship "Bandar Abbas-class replenishment ship") and its crew of 208 sailors was also interned in Sri Lanka following the proceedings.[^370]

#### Turkish airspace violation and NATO interception

A ballistic missile launched from Iranian territory was intercepted by [NATO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO "NATO") integrated air defense systems as it entered Turkish airspace, marking a significant escalation in the regional conflict.[^371] The projectile, initially detected by the [Kürecik Radar Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C3%BCrecik_Radar_Station "Kürecik Radar Station") in [Malatya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malatya "Malatya"), was neutralized by maritime interceptors stationed in the Eastern Mediterranean, with debris falling in the [Dörtyol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D%C3%B6rtyol "Dörtyol") district of [Hatay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hatay "Hatay"). While no casualties were reported, the [Turkish Ministry of National Defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Defence_\(Turkey\) "Ministry of National Defence (Turkey)") confirmed the engagement and reaffirmed its right to self-defense, noting that this was the first direct violation of a NATO member's territory during the ongoing hostilities.[^372]

Following the interception, reports from the [Wall Street Journal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wall_Street_Journal "Wall Street Journal") indicated that the missile’s trajectory was locked onto [Incirlik Air Base](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Incirlik_Air_Base "Incirlik Air Base") in [Adana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adana "Adana"), leading to heightened security measures around strategic installations. [Secretary General of NATO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secretary_General_of_NATO "Secretary General of NATO") [Mark Rutte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Rutte "Mark Rutte") condemned the breach, stating that the alliance remains "fully committed to the defense of Turkish soil," while [United States Secretary of Defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Defense "United States Secretary of Defense") [Pete Hegseth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pete_Hegseth "Pete Hegseth") emphasized that the interception demonstrated the "unwavering integration" of allied missile shields.[^373] In a diplomatic response, Iran officially denied intentionally targeting Turkey, attributing the event to a "technical anomaly." Despite these denials, the potential invocation of [NATO's Article 4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty#Article_4 "North Atlantic Treaty") became a focal point of urgent discussions between [Turkish Foreign Minister](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minister_of_Foreign_Affairs_\(Turkey\) "Minister of Foreign Affairs (Turkey)") [Hakan Fidan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hakan_Fidan "Hakan Fidan") and allied leadership, as Turkey sought to reinforce the alliance's collective defense posture in the face of further aerial threats.[^374]

#### Alleged Kurdish attacks

According to an unnamed official from the [Coalition of Political Forces of Iranian Kurdistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coalition_of_Political_Forces_of_Iranian_Kurdistan "Coalition of Political Forces of Iranian Kurdistan"), Iraqi-based Kurdish armed groups consisting of thousands of the [Kurdistan Free Life Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurdistan_Free_Life_Party "Kurdistan Free Life Party") (PJAK) troops had [begun a military offensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Kurdish_rebellion_in_Iran "2026 Kurdish rebellion in Iran") into Iranian territory, with operations beginning earlier on 2 March.[^375] American and Israeli officials reportedly confirmed the events.[^376] However, an unnamed PJAK official denied the claims of an ongoing offensive and cross-border troop movements, as did Aziz Ahmed, deputy chief of staff to Kurdistan Region's prime minister [Masrour Barzani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masrour_Barzani "Masrour Barzani").[^377] On 4 March, Trump held a phone call with Kurdish leaders in Iraq [Masoud Barzani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masoud_Barzani "Masoud Barzani") and [Bafel Talabani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bafel_Talabani "Bafel Talabani"), during which they discussed the next stages of war in Iran.[^378]

According to [*Axios*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axios_\(website\) "Axios (website)"), Barzani and Talabani expressed reservations about getting the [Peshmerga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peshmerga "Peshmerga") involved in any ground invasion on Iran,[^378] adding as a main cause of concern a massive military response from Iran against Kurdish forces in Iraq.[^379] Separately, Trump spoke with [Mustafa Hijri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustafa_Hijri "Mustafa Hijri"), a Kurdish leader in Iran.[^378] *Axios* reported that Secretary Rubio told Congress that the US was not arming the Kurds, but he added that "you never know with the Israelis." [^378] White House press secretary [Karoline Leavitt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karoline_Leavitt "Karoline Leavitt") said that President Trump had not decided whether to support the Kurds in a potential offensive, with Kurdish militants inside Iran saying that they are waiting the American "green light".[^378] The assembly of PJAK called on the people of Iranian Kurdistan to form "local governance committees" and "self-defence committees", to resist displacement by government forces and to stay away from their known locations for safety.[^380]

### 5 March

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Airstrike_on_12%2C000-seat_Azadi_Hall_33.jpg/250px-Airstrike_on_12%2C000-seat_Azadi_Hall_33.jpg)

Damage to Azadi Sport Complex on March 5, 2026

An American Israeli airstrike destroyed the 12,000-seat indoor arena at Tehran's [Azadi complex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azadi_Stadium "Azadi Stadium"). This came as it is known that authorities use several stadiums and sports centers in various cities to gather and station military and security forces, as well as equipment and vehicles, to shield them from US and Israeli strikes.[^381] Two [Basij](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basij "Basij") student leaders who had been involved in the [suppression of protests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iran_massacres "2026 Iran massacres") were killed in Israeli airstrikes.[^382]

On 5 March 2026, a military source told [Fars News Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fars_News_Agency "Fars News Agency") that Iran fired over 500 ballistic and naval missiles and almost 2,000 drones since 28 February. The report claimed that almost 40 percent of the launches were aimed towards Israel, and almost 60 percent were fired towards US targets in the region.[^383] Ukrainian President [Volodymyr Zelensky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volodymyr_Zelensky "Volodymyr Zelensky") stated that Ukraine has received an American request for assistance with Iranian [Shahed drones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shahed_drones "Shahed drones"). President Trump stated that he will accept Ukrainian assistance.[^384] [^385]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Armada_Espa%C3%B1ola_F105_Crist%C3%B3bal_Col%C3%B3n.jpg/250px-Armada_Espa%C3%B1ola_F105_Crist%C3%B3bal_Col%C3%B3n.jpg)

The frigate F105 Cristóbal Colón, sent by Spain to protect Cyprus from hypothetical further aerial threats against the island of Cyprus

During the visit of UK defence minister [John Healey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Healey "John Healey") no missiles were sent towards Cyprus, however, the alarms in British bases ringed twice causing widespread panic in the local population and self evacuations. Both times the bases confirmed that despite a rocket being launched, both of the time it did not end up being towards Cyrpus in the end.[^386] Meanwhile, Italy, the Netherlands and Spain confirmed that they would be sending warships to defend Cyprus,[^387] including the *[Cristóbal Colón](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_frigate_Crist%C3%B3bal_Col%C3%B3n "Spanish frigate Cristóbal Colón")* frigate.[^388]

#### Attack on Nakhchivan, Azerbaijan

Azerbaijan said that two drones from Iran struck Azerbaijan's [Nakhchivan exclave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nakhchivan_Autonomous_Republic "Nakhchivan Autonomous Republic").[^389] One drone struck the terminal building of [Nakhchivan International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nakhchivan_International_Airport "Nakhchivan International Airport"), while another landed near a school building in the village of Shakarabad, according to the [Ministry of Foreign Affairs of Azerbaijan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_\(Azerbaijan\) "Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Azerbaijan)"), damaging the airport and injuring two civilians.[^390] Azerbaijan summoned their Iranian ambassador [^391] and promised a military response.[^392]

Iran's foreign minister [Abbas Araghchi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbas_Araghchi "Abbas Araghchi") denied that Iran had attacked Azerbaijan, and suggested that it was an Israeli [false flag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/False_flag "False flag") attack.[^393] [Azer News](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Azer_News&action=edit&redlink=1 "Azer News (page does not exist)") reported that a Telegram channel affiliated with the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps, "Sepah Pasdaran News Channel", claimed responsibility for the attack in Nakhchivan.[^394] Azerbaijani president [Ilham Aliyev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilham_Aliyev "Ilham Aliyev") said that "Iran committed terror acts against Azerbaijan".[^395] Turkey likewise condemned the strikes in Azerbaijan.[^396]

## Strikes and casualties

### Iran

#### Assassination of Ali Khamenei

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Ali_Khamenei_2026.02.12_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Ali_Khamenei_2026.02.12_%28cropped%29.jpg)

Khamenei on 12 February 2026, 16 days before his assassination

On 28 February 2026, [Ali Khamenei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Khamenei "Ali Khamenei"), the [supreme leader of Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran "Supreme Leader of Iran"), was assassinated. Early on 1 March, Iranian state media announced that Khamenei had been killed.[^397] The [Fars News Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fars_News_Agency "Fars News Agency"), which is controlled by the IRGC, announced that Khamenei's daughter, son-in-law, grandchild, and daughter-in-law had also been killed in the strikes.[^398] [^399] [^400] The state declared 40 days of mourning.[^401] CIA assessments suggested that a hardliner from the IRGC would replace Khamenei.[^402]

#### Iranian military and officials

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Aziz_Nasirzadeh_%28February_2026%29.jpg/120px-Aziz_Nasirzadeh_%28February_2026%29.jpg)

Minister of Defence [Aziz Nasirzadeh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aziz_Nasirzadeh "Aziz Nasirzadeh")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/%D9%85%D8%AD%D9%85%D8%AF_%D9%BE%D8%A7%DA%A9%D9%BE%D9%88%D8%B11.jpg/120px-%D9%85%D8%AD%D9%85%D8%AF_%D9%BE%D8%A7%DA%A9%D9%BE%D9%88%D8%B11.jpg)

IRGC commander [Mohammad Pakpour](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Pakpour "Mohammad Pakpour")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Shamkhani.jpg/120px-Shamkhani.jpg)

Secretary of the Iranian Defence Council [Ali Shamkhani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Shamkhani "Ali Shamkhani")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/The_new_head_of_the_Basij_Organization_29_%28portrait_crop%29.jpg/250px-The_new_head_of_the_Basij_Organization_29_%28portrait_crop%29.jpg)

Head of the Military Office of the Supreme Leader of Iran [Mohammad Shirazi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Shirazi_\(general\) "Mohammad Shirazi (general)")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Iranian_drone_exercise_in_2022_-_Day_2_%2850%29.jpg/250px-Iranian_drone_exercise_in_2022_-_Day_2_%2850%29.jpg)

Chief of staff of the Iranian Armed Forces [Abdolrahim Mousavi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdolrahim_Mousavi "Abdolrahim Mousavi")

Reuters reported several commanders in the IRGC may have been killed, but could not confirm this report.[^403] It later reported, citing Israeli military and regional sources, that defence minister [Aziz Nasirzadeh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aziz_Nasirzadeh "Aziz Nasirzadeh") and IRGC commander [Mohammad Pakpour](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Pakpour "Mohammad Pakpour") had likely been killed by Israeli airstrikes.[^404] Iranian foreign minister [Abbas Araghchi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbas_Araghchi "Abbas Araghchi") acknowledged but downplayed the losses, deeming them "not such a big problem".[^405] Iran International reported that [Defence Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Defence_Council "Iranian Defence Council") secretary [Ali Shamkhani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Shamkhani "Ali Shamkhani") had been killed,[^406] along with four top [Ministry of Intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Intelligence_\(Iran\) "Ministry of Intelligence (Iran)") officials.[^407] The IDF later stated that it had confirmed the deaths of seven Iranian security leaders, including Shamkhani, Nasirzadeh, and Pakpour.[^408]

Additional senior officials confirmed to have been killed are [Salah Asadi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salah_Asadi "Salah Asadi"), head of intelligence for Iran's emergency command, [Mohammad Shirazi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Shirazi_\(general\) "Mohammad Shirazi (general)"), head of the military office of Khamenei, head of the [Organization of Defensive Innovation and Research](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organization_of_Defensive_Innovation_and_Research "Organization of Defensive Innovation and Research") (SPND) [Hossein Jabal Amelian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hossein_Jabal_Amelian "Hossein Jabal Amelian") and former SPND head [Reza Mozaffari Nia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reza_Mozaffari_Nia "Reza Mozaffari Nia").[^202] On 1 March, chief of staff [Abdolrahim Mousavi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdolrahim_Mousavi "Abdolrahim Mousavi") and former president [Mahmoud Ahmadinejad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad "Mahmoud Ahmadinejad") were confirmed by Iranian state media to have also been killed by strikes.[^409] [^410] However, later reports stated that Ahmadinejad is alive.[^411] [^412]

[CBS News](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CBS_News "CBS News") reported that "an intelligence source and a military source told CBS News Saturday evening \[28th February 2026\]" that 40 Iranian officials had been killed in the strikes but that they were not "clear whether these officials were in one location or multiple locations".[^413] [^414] [Iran's Foreign Ministry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_\(Iran\) "Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Iran)") stated the military has lost control over several units, that are operating according to old general instructions.[^415] On 4 March, [Hengaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hengaw "Hengaw") estimated that 2,100 members of Iranian military forces had been killed in the attacks.[^416]

#### Iranian civilians

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Shajareh_Tayyebeh_school_in_Minab_photos_from_Mehr_%283%29.jpg/250px-Shajareh_Tayyebeh_school_in_Minab_photos_from_Mehr_%283%29.jpg)

Rescuers and residents searching through the rubble of the destroyed girls' elementary school in Minab

At around 17:30 CET of the first day of strikes, the [Iranian Red Crescent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Red_Crescent_Society "Iranian Red Crescent Society") reported that 201 civilians had been killed and 747 injured in Iran, but this has not been independently confirmed.[^244] Two students were killed in a strike in [Tehran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tehran "Tehran"), according to Qatari-owned [Al Jazeera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Jazeera_Media_Network "Al Jazeera Media Network").[^417] A further 20 civilians were killed in Tehran's Niloofar Square on 2 March.[^418] On 3 March, the Red Crescent stated that over 600 civilians had been killed,[^419] while the [Human Rights Activists in Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Rights_Activists_in_Iran "Human Rights Activists in Iran") estimated that 742 civilians had been killed in the attacks.[^76]

[A girls' elementary school was hit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Minab_school_airstrike "2026 Minab school airstrike") in the Israeli and American attacks on [Minab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minab "Minab").[^420] with Iranian State-media reports stated that 148 students had been killed and 95 had been wounded in the strike.[^421] There is no independent confirmation of the number killed,[^422] [^208] although *[The Washington Post](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Washington_Post "The Washington Post")* and *The New York Times* verified footage taken immediately after the attack.[^423] [^424] A spokesperson for the Iranian foreign ministry called the strike a "war crime" by Israel, though Israel denied the attack and [CENTCOM](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CENTCOM "CENTCOM") confirmed it was investigating internally.[^425] Thousands of people attended the burial of the victims, according to Iranian state-owned media.[^312] *The New York Times* mentioned that the school was less than 60 meters from a large IRGC naval base, which was equipped with powerful anti-ship and anti-air missiles.[^424]

#### Iranian institutions

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Attack_on_Gandhi_Hospital_3.jpg/250px-Attack_on_Gandhi_Hospital_3.jpg)

Tehran's Gandhi Hospital was severely damaged on 1 March 2026, during a wave of U.S. and Israeli airstrikes targeting the Iranian capital.

The opening attack on 28 February targeted the compound of Leadership House. On 2 March 2026, video footage released by Iran International showed the IRGC Malek-Ashtar building in Tehran completely destroyed following a joint US Israel missile strike on the capital.[^426] In the early hours of 3 March 2026, the complex of the [Islamic Republic of Iran Broadcasting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Republic_of_Iran_Broadcasting "Islamic Republic of Iran Broadcasting") (IRIB), the state broadcaster's headquarters in Tehran, was hit in a separate Israeli air operation.[^427] [^428]

Iranian authorities reported that parts of the broadcaster's facilities were struck but no casualties were reported.[^429] [^430] Iranian state-linked media indicated that Iran's parliament building was also targeted by airstrikes.[^431] Trump told reporters that "Just about everything's been knocked out" and that Iran had no navy, air force, air detection, or radar after the attacks.[^148]

Israel bombed Iran's [Assembly of Experts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assembly_of_Experts "Assembly of Experts") as they were in a meeting to elect the next supreme leader.[^432] By 5 March, the World Health Organization had identified 13 attacks on Iranian health infrastructure by the US and Israel, as well as one attack on a health facility in Lebanon.[^433]

### Israel

The first connected Iranian airstrike targeted a building in Israel, leaving one Israeli civilian injured.[^434] [Magen David Adom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magen_David_Adom "Magen David Adom") reported that Iran's initial attacks had left 89 injured, with three directly wounded and the rest indirectly.[^435] On 28 February, a direct hit in [Tel Aviv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv "Tel Aviv") killed a woman and injured 22 others, one seriously.[^436] On 1 March, an Iranian strike hit a synagogue and residential buildings in [Beit Shemesh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beit_Shemesh "Beit Shemesh"), killing nine people and injuring 49 others.[^437] Israeli broadcaster [Kan 11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kan_11 "Kan 11") reported that 90, 65, and 25 missiles were launched at Israel from Iran on the first three days of the war, with 20 recorded in part of the fourth day.[^438]

### United States

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/US_casualities_Iran_attack_in_kuwait_March_1st_2026.jpg/250px-US_casualities_Iran_attack_in_kuwait_March_1st_2026.jpg)

First four of the six US soldiers killed in the war: Capt. Cody Khork, 35, of Winter Haven, Florida; Sgt. 1st Class Noah Tietjens, 42, of Bellevue, Nebraska; Sgt. 1st Class Nicole Amor, 39, of White Bear Lake, Minnesota; and Sgt. Declan Coady, 20, of West Des Moines, lowa.

On the first day of the war, [United States Central Command](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Central_Command "United States Central Command") (CENTCOM) initially stated that it had suffered no casualties, noting that light damage to its facilities had not disrupted its operations and that it had neutralized several hundred Iranian drone and missile strikes.[^439] At 9:30 a.m. ET on 1 March, CENTCOM confirmed that three US service members were killed and five others were seriously injured during the operation.[^48]

On 2 March, it was announced that US fatalities had risen to six, with four others seriously injured.[^440] Four of the victims have been identified, who are, according to CENTCOM, all members of the [103rd Sustainment Command (Expeditionary)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/103rd_Sustainment_Command_\(Expeditionary\) "103rd Sustainment Command (Expeditionary)"), headquartered in [Des Moines, Iowa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Des_Moines,_Iowa "Des Moines, Iowa").[^441] All 6 confirmed US fatalities were killed in a single Iranian airstrike on a base in Kuwait.[^442]

### Lebanon

By 2 March, Israel did a ground incursion in southern Lebanon with forces from the [91st Division](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/91st_Division_\(Israel\) "91st Division (Israel)") with the goal to stablish a "security layer" for the Israeli residents of northern settlements against the menace of Hezbollah, expecting to destroy their infrastructure in the [Israel-Lebanon border](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_Lebanon_border "Israel Lebanon border"). The [Lebanese government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanese_government "Lebanese government") reported that such Israeli [preventive attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Preventive_attack "Preventive attack") reached [Kfarkela](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kfarkela "Kfarkela") and [Qouzah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qaouzah "Al-Qaouzah"), provoking the [Lebanese army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanese_army "Lebanese army") to do a redeployment from newly established border posts amid escalating Israeli activity in violation of [2024 Israel–Lebanon ceasefire agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Israel%E2%80%93Lebanon_ceasefire_agreement "2024 Israel–Lebanon ceasefire agreement").[^443]

At least 31 people were killed [^444] and 149 were wounded by Israeli strikes in Lebanon,[^54] as well as three additional paramedics, according to Al Jazeera.[^71] Youssef Ragi, the Lebanese foreign minister, announced Lebanon's Council of Ministers decided to ban the military and security of Hezbollah, and called for them to hand over their weapons.[^445] Israel called for Lebanon to take action beyond mere statements.[^446] An NBC News analysis described Hezbollah as "significantly weakened".[^447]

### Other countries and regions

In addition to its strikes against Israel, Iran launched strikes against [Bahrain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iranian_strikes_on_Bahrain "2026 Iranian strikes on Bahrain"),[^448] [^449] [Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iranian_strikes_on_Kuwait "2026 Iranian strikes on Kuwait"),[^450] [Oman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iranian_strikes_on_Oman "2026 Iranian strikes on Oman"),[^451] [Saudi Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iranian_strikes_on_Saudi_Arabia "2026 Iranian strikes on Saudi Arabia"),[^452] [^453] [the United Arab Emirates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iranian_strikes_on_the_United_Arab_Emirates "2026 Iranian strikes on the United Arab Emirates"),[^454] [^455] [Azerbaijan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iran_strikes_on_Azerbaijan "2026 Iran strikes on Azerbaijan"),[^389] [^390] the [Kurdistan Region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iranian_strikes_on_the_Kurdistan_Region "2026 Iranian strikes on the Kurdistan Region") of Iraq,[^456] and the [Akrotiri and Dhekelia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iranian_strikes_on_Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia "2026 Iranian strikes on Akrotiri and Dhekelia") British Overseas Territory in Cyprus.[^457] Among the casualties are 3 Indian nationals killed in the strait of Hormuz,[^458] a Chinese national killed in Iran,[^75] and a Philippines national killed in Israel.[^459]

In Iraq, two members of the [Popular Mobilization Forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_Mobilization_Forces "Popular Mobilization Forces") were killed and three injured in a US-Israeli attack on 28 February.[^460] A later report from *The New York Times* claimed three dead.[^461] On 1 and 2 March, the United States and Israel conducted several attacks on Iranian-backed Iraqi militias to degrade their military capabilities to conduct retaliatory attacks.[^462] [^463] On 2 March, a Kuwaiti [F/A-18](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_F/A-18_Hornet "McDonnell Douglas F/A-18 Hornet") shot down three American [F-15Es](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/F-15E "F-15E") in a [friendly fire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friendly_fire "Friendly fire") incident. The six crew members survived. The [United States embassy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embassy_of_the_United_States,_Kuwait_City "Embassy of the United States, Kuwait City") in Kuwait was also hit by an Iranian missile strike, prompting Marco Rubio to close the embassy until further notice.[^279] [^278]
