## Impact

### Iranian politics

The [killing of Ali Khamenei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Killing_of_Ali_Khamenei "Killing of Ali Khamenei") led to the creation of an interim government, the [Interim Leadership Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interim_Leadership_Council "Interim Leadership Council"), on 1 March.[^251]

### State of emergency in Israel

Israel declared a nationwide [state of emergency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_of_emergency "State of emergency"), saying that the strikes on Iran were the largest that it had ever launched.[^198] [^475] Israel Katz issued a statement saying "Under my authority pursuant to Section 9C(b)(1) of the Civil Defence Law, 5711-1951, and after being convinced that there is a high probability of an attack on the civilian population, I hereby declare a special state on the home front throughout the entire territory of the country." [^476] Israeli schools and workspaces were closed and public gatherings were cancelled.[^89]

#### Gaza Strip

Because of the strikes and other safety concerns, the Israeli [Coordinator of Government Activities in the Territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coordinator_of_Government_Activities_in_the_Territories "Coordinator of Government Activities in the Territories") closed multiple aid crossings in the [Gaza Strip](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_Strip "Gaza Strip") (specifically interrupting free circulation on the [Egypt–Gaza border](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt%E2%80%93Gaza_border "Egypt–Gaza border")).[^477] Israeli forces suspended [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations") humanitarian movements and postponed planned rotations of international humanitarian staff (including medical evacuations and the return of people into Gaza), which the [United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Office_for_the_Coordination_of_Humanitarian_Affairs "United Nations Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs") condemned.[^478]

### Renewed internet blackout and suppression of Iranian civilians

Amid the renewed "near total" [internet blackout in Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Internet_blackout_in_Iran "2026 Internet blackout in Iran"), [NetBlocks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NetBlocks "NetBlocks") reported that internet connectivity in Iran dropped to 4% of ordinary levels.[^208] [^209] [^210] As news of Khamenei's death broke, many Iranians began pouring out into the streets in celebration, though security forces were deployed to prevent an uprising, with footage showing them opening fire on celebrants in the streets.[^479] [^480] Footage also showed security forces shooting at people chanting behind the windows of their homes.[^481] After Iran's foreign ministry spokesperson held a televised press conference from a classroom in Tehran, concerns grew over Iran's use of civilian sites.[^482] Footage also showed Iranian security forces stationed in schools and hospitals across the country.[^482] [^483]

### Prosecution of other civilians

The [Arab states of the Persian Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_states_of_the_Persian_Gulf "Arab states of the Persian Gulf") started a campaign of prosecution against civilians and foreign citizens that shared or reposted rumours from unverified sources about the Iranian attacks, with the stated main goal to curb misinformation that could harm public order.[^484] Bahrain's Cyber Crime Directorate also started a campaign of arresting civilians in the country, which has a large [Shiite minority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia_in_Bahrain "Shia in Bahrain"), who allegedly expressed "their support for the Iranian shelling targeting the Kingdom of Bahrain", describing such activities as treason and as promotion of hostile acts against the state.[^485]

### Disruption of daily life

As the US and Israel execute joint strikes targeting Iranian military and institutional targets, many cities have reportedly become ghost towns, as civilians fear going outside, or going about their daily jobs.[^486]

### Disruption of international trade and geopolitical impact

The [US–Israeli military strikes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iran_conflict "2026 Iran conflict") on [Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran "Iran") beginning 28 February 2026, and Iran's subsequent retaliatory actions, had global and regional economic consequences. The conflict led to immediate surges in [oil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Price_of_oil "Price of oil") and [gas prices](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_gas_prices "Natural gas prices"), widespread disruptions in aviation and tourism, declines in stock markets, and heightened volatility in financial markets. Analysts projected potential global inflation increases and risks of recession if disruptions persisted, particularly through [closures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Strait_of_Hormuz_crisis "2026 Strait of Hormuz crisis") of key shipping routes like the [Strait of Hormuz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strait_of_Hormuz "Strait of Hormuz").[^487] [^488] The strikes included the [assassination of Ali Khamenei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Ali_Khamenei "Assassination of Ali Khamenei") Iran's Supreme Leader, which involved millions of dollars in US military equipment, exacerbating economic uncertainties.[^489]

The conflict disrupted approximately 20% of global oil supplies transiting the Strait of Hormuz, causing prices on the [Brent Crude](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brent_Crude "Brent Crude") oil market to rise from around $70 to over $80 per barrel within days.[^490] Airspace closures in the [United Arab Emirates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates "United Arab Emirates") (UAE), [Qatar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar "Qatar"), [Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait "Kuwait"), and other Gulf states led to the grounding of thousands of flights, affecting major carriers like [Emirates Airlines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirates_Airlines "Emirates Airlines") and causing significant losses in tourism revenue.[^491] Stock markets experienced declines, with the [Dow Jones Industrial Average](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average "Dow Jones Industrial Average") falling over 400 points on 2 March.[^492] Broader economic forecasts warned of inflationary pressures and slowed global growth if the conflict prolonged.[^493]

#### Airspace closures

Iran's airspace was largely empty of civilian aircraft following the strikes as regional states closed airspace.[^494] [^495] Bahrain, Iraq, Israel, Kuwait, Qatar, Syria and the UAE closed their respective airspace following the attacks, with multiple [airliners](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airliner "Airliner") being redirected to other destinations.[^496] [^497] [^498] International airlines like [Air India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_India "Air India"), [Biman Bangladesh Airlines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biman_Bangladesh_Airlines "Biman Bangladesh Airlines"), [British Airways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Airways "British Airways"), [Cathay Pacific](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cathay_Pacific "Cathay Pacific"), [IndiGo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IndiGo "IndiGo"), [Lufthansa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lufthansa "Lufthansa"), [Virgin Atlantic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic "Virgin Atlantic"), and [Wizz Air](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wizz_Air "Wizz Air") suspended services to the Middle East in view of the war, as did airlines based in the region, including [Kuwait Airways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Airways "Kuwait Airways") and [Qatar Airways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar_Airways "Qatar Airways").[^499] [^500] [^501] [^502] According to a *[Wirtschaftswoche](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wirtschaftswoche "Wirtschaftswoche")* analysis, prolonging the conflict would mean a "catastrophe" for [Gulf states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_states_of_the_Persian_Gulf "Arab states of the Persian Gulf") such as Qatar and the UAE.[^503]

#### Strait of Hormuz

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hormuz_map.png/250px-Hormuz_map.png)

The Strait of Hormuz highlighted by a red arrow on the image

A Reuters report cited an [Operation Aspides](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Aspides "Operation Aspides") official who said that the IRGC had closed the [Strait of Hormuz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strait_of_Hormuz "Strait of Hormuz") to shipping, according to maritime [VHF](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/VHF "VHF") radio announcements. A [European Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union "European Union") official reported that vessels have been receiving messages stating that "no ship is allowed to pass the Strait of Hormuz".[^504] [^505] Late on 28 February, outgoing traffic was heavy, while ingoing traffic was light.[^506] Many vessels stayed outside the area, but some continued through. Three vessels were struck by projectiles, with partial damage,[^507] and an Iranian drone attack also killed a seafarer.[^508] [^260]

The current soft closure in Hormuz, alongside the fears of a declared blockade, has caused an increase in [financial risk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_risk "Financial risk") due to the impact in the prices for energy, shipping, insurance, aviation, etc. The war in the Persian Gulf theater has provoked [speculation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speculation "Speculation") in the [World economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_economy "World economy"), caused by the possibility of prolonged supply disruption, which will have broader consequences for [inflation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inflation "Inflation"), currencies, and emerging markets. One-fifth of global petroleum liquids consumption and more than one-quarter of global seaborne oil trade is done by the extraction of oil in the [Persian Gulf Basin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf_Basin "Persian Gulf Basin") and its commerce through crossing the [Strait of Hormuz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strait_of_Hormuz "Strait of Hormuz").[^509]

#### Strait of Bab-el-Mandeb

[Houthi-controlled Yemen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houthi-controlled_Yemen "Houthi-controlled Yemen") re-started its threats in the [Gulf of Aden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Aden "Gulf of Aden") and [Red Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Sea "Red Sea"), which had been suspended since 11 November 2025 after the [Gaza peace plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_peace_plan "Gaza peace plan") proposal.[^510] Houthis have been targeting commercial vessels (mainly the ones with business links to US or Israeli interests) through missile and drone operations against maritime traffic (in which other vessels could be targeted deliberately or in error) since the start of [Gaza war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_war "Gaza war").[^511]

Some security sources claim that Houthis are planning to do incursions in the [Arabian Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Sea "Arabian Sea") and also use bases from the African side of the Red Sea, helped by their presence and some cells established in [East Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Africa "East Africa").[^512] Danish carrier [Maersk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maersk "Maersk"), due to the risk situation in the [Bab-el-Mandeb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bab-el-Mandeb "Bab-el-Mandeb") strait, announced it was once again rerouting select services around the [Cape of Good Hope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope "Cape of Good Hope") route, instead of the [Suez Canal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Canal "Suez Canal") one, to reach the [Indian Ocean trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Ocean_trade "Indian Ocean trade").[^513]

#### European mobilization in Cyprus and Eastern Mediterranean

Following strikes on the island of Cyprus and the threats of the IRGC against the island, numerous nations [^294] —including France,[^514] Greece and the United Kingdom—decided to mobilize their armed forces in the surrounding waters and onto the island,[^515] vowing to protect it in case of an attack. The [European Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Commission "European Commission") Chief Spokesperson [Paula Pinho](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paula_Pinho "Paula Pinho") stated that in the coming days following the attack the EU "mutual defence clause will be up for discussion".[^516] The President of the [European People's Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_People%27s_Party "European People's Party") (EPP), [Manfred Weber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manfred_Weber "Manfred Weber"), called Iran a "criminal regime" and vowed that an attack on the Republic of Cyprus would be considered an attack on Europe.[^517]

Iran's response was to state that such acts of involvement in the conflict could be considered "acts of war",[^323] [^324] however analysts note that the European mobilization in Cyprus was not the reaction Iran expected and seems to have worked as a deterrent.[^518] Observers in the countries of Cyprus and Greece noted how the war was perceived pretty vividly and fears of further escalation involving both nations is prevalent.[^519] Cyprus expressed worries of possible terroristic cells that could act within the nations on Iran's behalf from [Northern Cyprus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Cyprus "Northern Cyprus"), where 10,000 pro‑regime Iranians live and where, allegedly, Hamas and the [Muslim Brotherhood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_Brotherhood "Muslim Brotherhood") operate.[^520]

Italy's [intelligence agencies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_intelligence_agencies "Italian intelligence agencies") have been reporting that it's highly possible that all the [Eastern Mediterranean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean "Eastern Mediterranean") region will be affected by the growing instability in the [Levant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levant "Levant") and the [Strait of Hormuz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strait_of_Hormuz "Strait of Hormuz"), mainly suffering impacts on energy markets and supply security, which will impact the [Mediterranean countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_countries "Mediterranean countries") and [Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Europe "Europe") as a whole if the [Indo-Mediterranean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Mediterranean "Indo-Mediterranean") trade route through [Suez Canal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Canal "Suez Canal") - [Red Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Sea "Red Sea") is damaged by the conflict (specially if [Houthis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houthis "Houthis") do a more active aid to Iran at the [Gulf of Aden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Aden "Gulf of Aden")), generating a widening arc of instability across the multiple regions of [Afro-Eurasia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afro-Eurasia "Afro-Eurasia"). Such catastrophic [Geopolitical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geopolitics "Geopolitics") possibility of maritime insecurity have been declared as the main reason of various [Western](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_world "Western world") countries to deploy troops with the main goal of protect the Euro- [Atlantic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean "Atlantic Ocean") trade routes.[^521] Also Italian prime minister, [Giorgia Meloni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giorgia_Meloni "Giorgia Meloni"), have been developing an approachment between the [European Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union "European Union") and the [Gulf Cooperation Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council "Gulf Cooperation Council") to do a common diplomatic strategy concerning the Iran-US conflict and mantain their neutrality while condemning Iranian attacks.[^522] [^523]

### Exodus of people

Tens of thousands of people within the [Gulf region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_states_of_the_Persian_Gulf "Arab states of the Persian Gulf") are stuck with few ways to leave.[^71] The [US](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States"), [UK](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom "United Kingdom"), [Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germany "Germany"), [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France "France"), [Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italy "Italy"), [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China"), and [Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poland "Poland") urged citizens to leave [Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran "Iran") and the [Gulf states (Middle East)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_states_\(Middle_East\) "Gulf states (Middle East)").[^524]

The [US Department of State](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US_Department_of_State "US Department of State") urged Americans in the Middle East to leave such countries due to "safety risks" as the war could last from four to five weeks or even more, recommending its population to use the available [commercial transportation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transit_privatization "Transit privatization").[^525] The [United States Department of State](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State "United States Department of State") subsequently announced it was working on bringing Americans in the Middle East home, and stated they are in contact with more than 3,000 Americans there.[^54]

According to Trump [^54] and Rubio, almost 9,000 Americans have evacuated from the Middle East since the start of the strikes.[^71] A US state department official stated many more Americans are expected to evacuate.[^526] The United Kingdom's [Foreign Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_Office "Foreign Office") said it was developing plans to evacuate UK citizens in the region.[^527] [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia "Russia"), through its [embassy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Russia "List of diplomatic missions of Russia"), made facilitations for Russians unable to leave Iran by liberalizing the route in the [Iran–Turkmenistan border](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Turkmenistan_border "Iran–Turkmenistan border").[^528] The [Foreign Ministry of Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_Ministry_of_Italy "Foreign Ministry of Italy") also helped to evacuate it's citizens from the [Gulf Countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Countries "Gulf Countries"), expecting to evacuate 30,000 italians at [UAE](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates "United Arab Emirates"),[^529] receiving in March 3 around 300 people from [Oman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oman "Oman") and other 200 from the UAE.[^530]

[Kazakhstan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kazakhstan "Kazakhstan") 's Foreign Ministry started to develop plans for evacuation measures to help [its nationals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kazakhs "Kazakhs") who were living in escalation zones, exploring routes through the [Caucasus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus "Caucasus"), [Turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey "Turkey") or [Central Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia "Central Asia").[^531] People started to leave the country through Azerbaijan's [Astara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astara_District "Astara District") crossing.[^531] [^532] Also increased the border crossing between Iran's [Mirjaveh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mirjaveh_County "Mirjaveh County") and [Taftan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taftan_County "Taftan County") to Pakistan's [Balochistan province](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balochistan_province "Balochistan province") by [Pakistanis in Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistanis_in_Iran "Pakistanis in Iran").[^533] However, the UN refugee agency stated there has been no major exodus from Iran.[^534] [^535] The UAE announced its intent to repatriate 44,000 travelers.[^71]

### Internet infrastructure

Three [Amazon Web Services](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amazon_Web_Services "Amazon Web Services") data centers were struck and damaged as a result of [drone strikes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drone_strikes "Drone strikes"), leading to outages of web infrastructure within the Middle East.[^536] Two data centers were directly targeted within the United Arab Emirates, causing "sparks and fire" as well as "major structural damage", with internal water levels reaching up to 4 cm, alongside the mechanical failure of cooling and air systems.[^537] Meanwhile, a data centre within Bahrain was indirectly damaged by a drone strike on nearby infrastructure.[^538] As the targeted data centres within the United Arab Emirates were in different [availability zones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Availability_zone "Availability zone"), and [Amazon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amazon_\(company\) "Amazon (company)") infrastructure was only designed to withstand redundancy of a single zone,[^539] fundamental web infrastructure including [S3 storage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amazon_S3 "Amazon S3"), [EC2 compute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amazon_Elastic_Compute_Cloud "Amazon Elastic Compute Cloud") and [DynamoDB databases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amazon_DynamoDB "Amazon DynamoDB") suffered complete outages within the Middle Eastern region.[^537]

### Food distribution

Reports have emerged that prisoners in [Evin Prison](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evin_Prison "Evin Prison") have been receiving limited bread and water since the onset of the war.[^540]

## Reactions

### Iran

#### Government

[Iran's foreign ministry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_\(Iran\) "Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Iran)") vowed a response as Iranian forces struck US bases across the [Persian Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf "Persian Gulf").[^223] [^541] The [Supreme National Security Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_National_Security_Council "Supreme National Security Council") said Iran was targeted by a "brutal air operation" carried out by the US and Israel, saying: "This occurred once again during negotiations, and the enemy imagines that the resilient Iranian nation will surrender to their petty demands through these cowardly actions." [^48] Abbas Araghchi called the attacks "wholly unprovoked, illegal, and illegitimate".[^501]

#### Civilians

A holistic picture of civilian reactions in Iran is somewhat difficult to obtain due to the [government's control over the circulation of information](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Censorship_in_Iran "Censorship in Iran"), the [renewed internet blackout](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Internet_blackout_in_Iran#Renewed_blackout "2026 Internet blackout in Iran"), and the ongoing heated nature of the war.[^542] *[The Daily Telegraph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph "The Daily Telegraph")* and Iran International posted videos of some people inside Iran celebrating the attacks, hopeful that they will bring forth an end to the ruling government.[^543] [^544] *The New York Times*, Reuters, Al Jazeera, and [Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_Free_Europe/Radio_Liberty "Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty") published photos of some Iranians during pro-government rallies waving the [Islamic Republic flag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flag_of_Iran "Flag of Iran") holding portraits of Khamenei while demonstrating against the US and Israeli attack.[^89] [^545] [^546] [^547] As news of Khamenei's death broke, many Iranians began pouring out into the streets in celebration, though security forces were deployed to prevent an uprising, with footage showing them opening fire on celebrants in the streets.[^548] [^479] [^480] Footage also showed security forces [shooting at people chanting behind the windows of their homes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2025%E2%80%932026_Iranian_protests#After_the_strikes "2025–2026 Iranian protests").[^481]

#### Diaspora and opposition

Following the US–Israeli airstrikes on Iran, [Iranians living abroad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_diaspora "Iranian diaspora") showed support for regime change in Iran. [Celebratory rallies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iranian_diaspora_protests#Following_the_Israeli%E2%80%93United_States_strikes_on_Iran "2026 Iranian diaspora protests") were held worldwide by the Iranian diaspora, where Iranians gathered waving anti-Islamic Republic symbols, including the [Lion and Sun flag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lion_and_Sun_flag "Lion and Sun flag").[^549] [^550] [^551] [Reza Pahlavi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reza_Pahlavi "Reza Pahlavi"), a leader of the [opposition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_opposition "Iranian opposition") and son of the former [Shah of Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shah_of_Iran "Shah of Iran"), is supportive of Israel and the US, and states he is ready to have his transitional government take over if the Islamic Republic is overthrown.[^552] [^553]

### United States

Donald Trump confirmed that the US military had begun "major combat operations" in Iran,[^554] describing it as "a massive and ongoing operation to prevent this very wicked, radical dictatorship from threatening America".[^555] In a video posted to [Truth Social](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truth_Social "Truth Social"), he reaffirmed that "Our objective is to defend the American people by eliminating imminent threats from the Iranian regime, a vicious group of very hard, terrible people", adding: "For 47 years, the Iranian regime has chanted 'Death to America' and waged an unending campaign of bloodshed and mass murder, targeting the United States, our troops and the innocent people in many, many countries." [^556] Trump said that talks with Iran will be easier following Khamenei's assassination.[^202] On the third day of the war, Trump said that the US military is "knocking the crap out of Iran but the big wave of attacks yet to come" and mentioning the possible use of ground troops.[^202] According to experts, the use of ground troops are required for the goals of the Trump administration in the middle east.[^557] On 3 March, Trump said on Truth Social: "Their air defense, Air Force, Navy, and Leadership is gone. They want to talk. I said, 'Too Late!' " [^148] Trump claimed victory and said that he had defeated Iran militarily.[^54]

#### Public

[Opinion polling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opinion_polling "Opinion polling") showed that most Americans were unsupportive of US military action against Iran.[^558] According to *[The Guardian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guardian "The Guardian")*, 27% of Americans were supportive of the US operation while 43% were opposed and 29% were uncertain.[^559] Most Americans reported they believe that Trump still has not explained the goals behind attacking Iran.[^441] Polls showed splits on the issue on political and demographic lines. Most Republicans supported the action, while most Democrats and independents opposed it.[^558] Trump reacted to the disapproval by denying that opinion polling showed low approval ratings, also adding, "I don't care about polling." [^560] [^561]

#### Politicians

Some members of the US congress called for a vote on the [War Powers Resolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_Powers_Resolution "War Powers Resolution"), also known as the War Powers Act,[^562] that some other members asserted could have effectively ended the attack on Iran.[^563] [Mike Johnson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Johnson "Mike Johnson"), the [Speaker of the United States House of Representatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives "Speaker of the United States House of Representatives"), called the vote "dangerous".[^441] The resolution failed,[^564] mainly due to Republicans.[^565] Congress member [Thomas Massie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Massie "Thomas Massie") and former congress member [Marjorie Taylor Greene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marjorie_Taylor_Greene "Marjorie Taylor Greene") said that Trump started the war as a distraction from [ongoing disclosures relating to the Epstein pedophile network](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epstein_files "Epstein files").[^566] The resolution was blocked by the Senate.[^567]

### Israel

Netanyahu said the goal of the strikes was to "remove the existential threat posed by the terrorist regime in Iran", stating that "our joint action will create the conditions for the brave Iranian people to take their destiny into their own hands." [^568] Foreign Minister [Gideon Sa'ar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gideon_Sa%27ar "Gideon Sa'ar") said that military action against Iran was urgently needed "despite the significant risks involved", adding that "delay would have allowed the Iranian regime to reach a level of immunity for its nuclear programme, as well as to engage in the mass production of long-range ballistic missiles".[^569] Minister of Science and Technology [Gila Gamliel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gila_Gamliel "Gila Gamliel") said that [2026 Israeli legislative election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Israeli_legislative_election "2026 Israeli legislative election") will likely be brought forward to late June or July to allow Netanyahu bloc to leverage the war.[^570] On 4 March 2026, Defence Minister Israel Katz disclosed that Israel had initially planned to strike Iran in mid-2026.[^571] On 5 March 2026, Katz said that Netanyahu set aim of assassinating supreme leader Ali Khamenei in November 2025.[^572]

### International

It was reported that European Union Commission president ⁠ [Ursula von der Leyen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ursula_von_der_Leyen "Ursula von der Leyen") supports a regime change in Iran.[^573] [^574] NATO secretary general [Mark Rutte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Rutte "Mark Rutte"), said that Europe is "supportive" of the US attacks on Iran, as Iran is a "threat".[^575] He also said that he felt that the US "knows what it is doing".[^576] The Israeli and US attacks were supported at least in part by Ukraine,[^577] [^578] Albania,[^579] Argentina,[^580] Australia,[^581] Canada,[^582] Czechia,[^583] Finland,[^584] Germany,[^585] Kosovo,[^586] Latvia,[^587] Lithuania,[^587] New Zealand,[^588] Papua New Guinea,[^589] Romania,[^587] and Trinidad and Tobago,[^590] while being implicitly or explicitly opposed by Afghanistan,[^591] Armenia,[^592] Brazil,[^593] Chile,[^594] [^595] China,[^596] Kazakhstan,[^597] [^598] Oman,[^599] North Korea,[^600] Norway,[^578] Malaysia,[^601] Pakistan,[^602] Russia,[^577] and Vietnam.[^603]

Iran's retaliations were condemned by Austria,[^587] Bahrain,[^599] Belgium,[^587] Bulgaria,[^587] incoming president of Chile [José Antonio Kast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Antonio_Kast "José Antonio Kast"),[^604] Croatia,[^587] Cyprus,[^587] Djibouti,[^605] Egypt,[^606] India,[^607] [^608] Kazakhstan,[^597] Kuwait,[^578] Malta,[^587] Morocco,[^609] Netherlands,[^587] the Palestinian Authority,[^610] Portugal,[^611] Qatar,[^578] Saudi Arabia,[^232] Sweden,[^587] Syria,[^612] Somalia,[^613] Turkey,[^71] the UAE,[^578] as well as by France, Germany, and the United Kingdom, who issued a joint declaration.[^614] Additionally, the United Kingdom permitted the US to use British military bases for defensive purposes,[^615] France sent its aircraft carrier towards the Mediterranean,[^71] and when asked whether they would join the war, Canada said they "can't rule out participation".[^616] On 5 March 2026, French broadcaster [BFMTV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BFM_TV "BFM TV") reported that France authorized American armed forces to use French bases amid the war.[^617] The partially recognised states of [Somaliland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Somaliland "Somaliland"),[^618] and [Taiwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan"),[^619] also condemned Iran's attacks on the gulf states.

Mixed reactions or calls for peace were made by South Africa,[^620] Azerbaijan,[^621] Indonesia,[^622] Lebanon,[^623] [^624] [^578] Ireland,[^625] Slovenia,[^587] Vatican City,[^626] Uruguay,[^627] Uzbekistan,[^628] and Venezuela.[^629] In addition to condemning both the Israeli and US attacks and Iran's counterattacks,[^587] Spain denied the use of its military bases for US flights connected to a military offensive against Iran, leading President Trump to threaten economic retaliation.[^630] In Pakistan, the [Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_Army "Pakistan Army") was deployed to supress the escalation of violence during [pro-Iranian protests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pro-Iranian_protests_during_the_2026_Israeli%E2%80%93United_States_strikes_on_Iran "Pro-Iranian protests during the 2026 Israeli–United States strikes on Iran") in the [northern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Pakistan "Northern Pakistan") cities of [Gilgit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilgit "Gilgit") and [Skardu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skardu "Skardu"), especially after Shiite demonstrators attacked on 1 March the offices of the [UN Military Observer Group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UN_Military_Observer_Group_for_India_and_Pakistan "UN Military Observer Group for India and Pakistan") at [Azad Kashmir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azad_Kashmir "Azad Kashmir"). Similar action was done in [Sindh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sindh "Sindh") during the [attack on the US consulate in Karachi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_attack_on_the_United_States_consulate_in_Karachi "2026 attack on the United States consulate in Karachi").[^631]

[^84]: ["How Trump Decided to Go to War"](https://www.nytimes.com/2026/03/02/us/politics/trump-war-iran-israel.html?unlocked_article_code=1.QVA.pkuR.UJsI_ed0iTWq). *[The New York Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_New_York_Times "The New York Times")*. 3 March 2026. There were few voices lobbying against military action. One exception was Tucker Carlson, the right-wing podcaster and close ally of the president, who has met with him in the Oval Office three times in the past month to argue against an attack. He outlined the risks to U.S. military personnel, energy prices and Arab partners in the region if the United States went to war with Iran. He told the president that he should not be boxed in by Israel, arguing that its desire to attack Iran was the only reason the United States was even considering a strike. He encouraged Mr. Trump to restrain Mr. Netanyahu. The president said he understood the risks of an attack, but he conveyed to Mr. Carlson that he had no choice but to join a strike that Israel would launch. After Mr. Carlson left the White House midday on Feb. 23, he told others he thought Mr. Trump was leaning toward military action.

[^112]: [" 'Deeply ideological': the rationale behind Iran's insistence on uranium enrichment"](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2026/jan/30/rationale-behind-iran-uranium-enrichment-nuclear-ambitions). *The Guardian*. Retrieved 5 March 2026. Asked by the Guardian in November in Tehran what cost benefit analysis could possibly conclude that the nuclear programme was a worthwhile project, the foreign minister, Abbas Araghchi, referred to Iran's sovereign right under the nuclear non-proliferation treaty, the medical benefits, and the blood of previously assassinated Iranian nuclear scientists. He suggested a compromise whereby a consortium including possibly the US could enrich uranium in Iran, but insisted the principle that uranium would be enriched inside Iran remained sacrosanct. Indeed, Ali Ansari, a professor of modern history at St Andrews University, says: 'Those people looking for a rational explanation for Iran's attachment to nuclear enrichment are not going to find it. It is deeply ideological, almost an obsession with national prestige. It is about making a point and riding the crest of an ultra-nationalist wave. It also serves a political purpose, including highlighting the unfairness of the west and so nursing a grievance. But the refusal to compromise means that the Iranian economy is being run into the ground for no practical purpose. The government tries to argue that what is being pursued is a national right, but this is incongruous because it is being pursued at the expense of other civil and human rights that Iranians could enjoy, including better schools and hospitals.'

A long-time victim of Russian, British and then American imperialism, the Iranian state has always sought independence. A rejection of US political and military domination became so much a given that the taking hostage of 52 US diplomats on 4 November 1979 was seen as a victory in a virtual 'war of independence' that ultimately backfired on Iran. During the cold war, this nationalist and pietist struggle was seen as support for the USSR and generated radical and enduring ideological hostility between Iran and the US. This bilateral war has been central to most regional wars and conflicts, and its political resolution remains the keystone of Middle East security.
